Proof that Every Originated Thing Needs a Creator
Dardeer proves the need for an originator via craftsmanship and the impossibility of self-causation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that every originated thing requires an originator, and why self-origination is impossible due to the need for a preponderator.

Core Idea
Every created thing points to a Creator; self-origination is self-contradictory.

This lesson presents the core of the kalam cosmological argument: the observable world displays perfect craftsmanship, which necessitates a maker. Dardeer then demonstrates that if something were to originate itself, it would have to give preponderance to existence over non-existence without any cause—an impossibility. He also addresses a nuance about the equality of existence and non-existence and the role of revelation for unseen entities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the logical structure: the claim, the evidence, the objection, and the resolution.
The passage is dense; read carefully.
2
Identify the main argument
Identify the core claim: every originated thing requires an originator. Spot the evidence from craftsmanship ('صنعة بديعة محكمة الإتقان') and the reasoning that if no maker, then self-origination leads to absurdity.
The absurdity is highlighted by the terms 'ترجيح', 'مساواة', and 'مرجح'.
3
Analyze the impossibility of self-origination
Understand the logical contradiction: self-origination would require preponderance of existence over non-existence without a cause, which is impossible because it entails the conjunction of opposites (equality and preponderance).
This is a key metaphysical principle in kalam.
4
Examine the refinement about strength
Consider the footnote: non-existence is the original state, so it is stronger than existence. This makes self-origination even more impossible. Also note the role of revelation for unobservable entities.
The footnote corrects the assumption of true equality between existence and non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دليلُ كَونِ كلَّ حادث فهو مُفتَقِرُ إلى مُوجِدٍ يوجده، فلأنه صنعةٌ بديعةٌ مُحَكَمةٌ الإتقان، وكُلّ ما كانَ كذلك فله صانع، إذ لو لم يكنْ له صانع للَزِمَ أَنْ يكونَ حَدَثَ بنفسِه، فيلزَمُ ترجيحُ أحدِ الأَمْرَينِ المُتساويين – أعني: الوُجودَ والعَدَمَ- على مُساويه بلا سبب، وهو مُحال؛ لما يلزَمُ عليه مِنَ اجتماع الضَّدَّين، أعني: المساواة والترجيح بلا مُرَجّح. على أنه يلزَمُ عليه ترجيح الأضعف على الأقوى (۲)؛ لأنَّ الأَصْلَ فيه العدَمُ، وهو أَقوى مِنْ وُجوده. (۲) هذا إضراب منه على ما قدمه من دعوى المساواة بين الأمرين، مع أنه في الواقع لا مساواة، وذلك لأن العدم أصل والوجود طارئ عليه، ومعلوم أن الأصل أقوى من الذي حدث بعده، وهذا ظاهر في الاستدلال على ما شوهد من العالم، وأما ما لم يشاهد كالارواح والعقول والمجردات على القول بها - فيكفي في حدوثها السمع، كقوله تعالى: والله خالق كل شيء) [الزمر : ٦٢] =
As for the proof that every originated thing is in need of an originator that brings it into existence: because it is a wonderful, perfectly crafted work, and everything like that has a maker. For if it had no maker, it would necessarily have originated by itself, which would require the preponderance of one of two equal alternatives—namely existence and non-existence—over its equal without cause, and that is impossible because it entails the conjunction of opposites, namely equality and preponderance without a preponderator. Moreover, it would entail the preponderance of the weaker over the stronger (2); because the original state is non-existence, which is stronger than its existence. (2) This is a retraction from him regarding the previous claim of equality between the two states, while in reality there is no equality. This is because non-existence is original and existence is accidental to it, and it is known that the original is stronger than what occurs after it. This is apparent in reasoning about what is observed of the world. As for what is not observed, like spirits, intellects, and abstract entities according to those who affirm them—the revealed law suffices for their origination, as His saying: 'And Allah is the Creator of all things' (Quran 39:62).
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents the second part of the kalam cosmological argument: proof that every originated thing needs a creator. The author argues based on craftsmanship: the world displays perfect design, so it must have a maker. If it originated without a maker, that would be self-origination, which leads to absurdity. The absurdity is that existence and non-existence are equal possibilities for a thing in itself; if it brings itself into existence, it would have to prefer existence over non-existence without any cause, which is impossible. This would also mean giving preponderance to the weaker over the stronger, because non-existence is the original state and is stronger (more fundamental) than existence. The footnote (2) clarifies that the claim of equality between existence and non-existence is not strictly true: non-existence is original and stronger, so the impossibility of self-origination is even more evident. For unobservable entities like spirits or intellects, the author notes that revelation (sam') is sufficient proof of their origination, citing Quran 39:62.

Key Terms
مفتقر
موجد
صنعة
صانع
ترجيح
مساواة
مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The world could have come into existence by itself without a cause.
Correction: The argument shows that self-origination is logically impossible because it would require an unexplained preponderance of existence over non-existence.

Checkpoint
Why is it impossible for an originated thing to have originated by itself?
A) Because it would require a prior cause
B) Because it would require preponderance of existence over non-existence without a preponderator
C) Because it would violate the laws of physics
D) Because it would be a miracle

Key Takeaway
The existence of a Creator is rationally necessary because every originated thing requires a cause, and self-origination is logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the world around you, do you see it as a perfectly crafted work requiring a Maker, or do you take it for granted? What would change in your daily life if you truly internalized that every moment of your existence is a gift from a Creator who chose to bring you into being over non-existence?
?
The argument shows that self-origination is logically impossible. Yet, how often do you live as though you are the source of your own existence and success? In what areas of your life are you acting as if you don't need a Creator, and how can you return to acknowledging His role as the Originator?
?
The passage acknowledges that for unseen realities we rely on revelation. Do you trust Allah's revelation more than your own reasoning when it comes to matters beyond your perception? Is your heart truly convinced that Allah is the Creator of all things, or is that just a mental assent without deep conviction?

Proof: Contingents Need a Creator
Dardir argues for the necessity of a creator for contingent things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why every contingent thing must have a creator, based on the impossibility of self-causation and the principle of preponderance.

Core Idea
A contingent thing cannot bring itself into existence without implying a logical contradiction.

In this passage, Imam Dardir completes the first proof of God's existence by showing that the contingent world, which is a perfectly crafted product, cannot have come into existence by itself. The argument hinges on the impossibility of one of two equally possible states (existence and non-existence) being chosen without a cause. Let's read the Arabic and unpack its logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic Passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the logical flow: observation of perfection → need for maker → self-creation absurd.
Pay attention to the terms 'صانع' (maker) and 'ترجيح' (preponderance).
2
Identify the Core Premise
The key premise is that everything that is a wonderful, precise craftsmanship has a maker. Dardir takes this as a given rational principle.
3
Understand the Impossibility Argument
Follow the reasoning: if no maker, then self-creation, which requires preponderance without cause, leading to contradiction (equality and preponderance). Also note the additional point about the weaker preponderating over the stronger.
Self-creation would mean existence was chosen over non-existence without any reason, which is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دليلُ كَونِ كلَّ حادث فهو مُفتَقِرُ إلى مُوجِدٍ يوجده، فلأنه صنعةٌ بديعةٌ مُحَكَمةٌ الإتقان، وكُلّ ما كانَ كذلك فله صانع، إذ لو لم يكنْ له صانع للَزِمَ أَنْ يكونَ حَدَثَ بنفسِه، فيلزَمُ ترجيحُ أحدِ الأَمْرَينِ المُتساويين – أعني: الوُجودَ والعَدَمَ- على مُساويه بلا سبب، وهو مُحال؛ لما يلزَمُ عليه مِنَ اجتماع الضَّدَّين، أعني: المساواة والترجيح بلا مُرَجّح. على أنه يلزَمُ عليه ترجيح الأضعف على الأقوى
As for the proof that every contingent is in need of an originator that brings it into existence: it is because it is a wonderful, perfectly precise craftsmanship, and everything that is like that has a maker. For if it had no maker, then it would have to have come into existence by itself, and that would necessitate the preponderance of one of two equal alternatives — namely, existence and non-existence — over its equal without cause, and that is impossible because of the consequent contradiction of two opposites, namely: equality and preponderance without a preponderator. Moreover, it would necessitate the preponderance of the weaker over the stronger.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage provides the second part of the standard kalam proof: that the contingent world requires a creator. The argument begins with the observation that the world is a perfectly crafted product (ṣanʿa badīʿa muḥkama). Anything so well‑made must have a maker. If it had no maker, it would have to bring itself into existence. But that would mean that from a state of equal possibility (existence and non‑existence), existence was chosen without any cause. This is impossible because it would combine equality and preponderance — a contradiction. Additionally, since non‑existence is the original and stronger state, preferring existence (the weaker) would be even more absurd. Thus the contingent world must have a creator.

Key Terms
صانع
ترجيح
مرجح
محال
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument assumes the world is exactly like a human artifact, so it's a weak analogy.
Correction: The argument uses the observed order and precision in the world to infer a maker, not a literal comparison to human artifacts. It is a rational necessity that any perfectly precise craftsmanship has a maker.

Checkpoint

A) It would remain nonexistent.
B) It would be eternal.
C) It would have to create itself, leading to an impossible preponderance without a preponderator.
D) It would be created by another contingent.

Key Takeaway
The perfection of the contingent world necessitates a creator, because self-creation would require an impossible choice without a cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You see the intricate design of your own body—your heart beating, your eyes seeing. Can you honestly tell yourself that all of this came into existence without a Creator? If not, what is holding you back from acknowledging Him in your daily life?
?
The argument proves that self-creation is impossible because it would require a choice without reason. Are there areas in your life where you live as if you are self-sufficient, ignoring your absolute dependence on your Creator? Will you consciously acknowledge that dependence today?
?
If every contingent thing needs a creator, then you yourself are a contingent being. What does that mean for your purpose and accountability? Are you living in a way that reflects your status as a creature created by a wise Maker?

The Diversity Proof for Contingency
Dardir presents a proof from the world's diversity and draws its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the world's diversity of types proves its contingency and the Creator's free choice.

Core Idea
Diversity demands a specificator; blind causes cannot produce variety.

Imam Dardir now offers a second, independent proof for the world's contingency: the striking diversity observed within creation. This argument, rooted in both reason and Quranic indication, shows that the variegation of types cannot arise from a necessary cause or nature, but requires a wise, free-choosing Creator. The passage also connects this diversity to the earlier well-known proof, setting the stage for further rational and revealed confirmations.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening lines
Start by reading the first few sentences where Dardir introduces this as an additional proof from diversity. Notice how he links it to the well-known proof.
The phrase 'ولك أن تستدل' indicates this is an optional but valid proof.
2
Examine the list of opposites
Review the pairs (celestial/terrestrial, luminous/dark, etc.) and understand that each type contains countless subtypes. Ask yourself: could a blind nature produce such ordered variety?
The sheer complexity points to a specificator.
3
Follow the conclusion
Read how Dardir concludes that the diversity necessitates a wise Specificator, making the world contingent and the Creator a free chooser, not a cause or nature.
The inference is that uniformity would be expected from necessity, not diversity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا هو البرهان المشهور بينهم في بيان حدوث العالم وافتقاره إلى صانع. ولك أن تستدلَّ على حدوثه بكونه أنواعًا مُختلفةً وأصْنافًا مُتباينة، كما يُشير إليه آي القرآن العزيز، وذلك لأنّ بعضه عُلويّ، وبعضه سفلي، وبعضه نوراني، وبعضه ظلماني، وبعضه حار، وبعضَه بارد، وبعضه متحرّك، وبعضه ساكن، وبعضه لطيف وبعضه كثيف، وبعضه شُوهِدَ وُجوده بعد عدَمه، وبعضه شُوهِدَ عَدَمُه بعد وجوده إلى غير ذلك. وكُلُّ نَوعِ مِنْ هذه الأنواع مُشْتَمِلٌ على أصناف وأفراد وصفات، لا قدرة لأحمد على إحصائها، فدل على أنه مُفْتَقِرٌ إلى مخصص حكيم، خص كُلَّ نَوع ببعض الحجاب عليه، فيكون حادثًا بعد عدَم، وأنَّ خالقه مُختار لا عِلة ولا طبيعةً، إذ معلول العلة ومطبوع الطبيعةِ لا يختَلِفُ على فرْضِ تسليمه. قال تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الَّيلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لآيات﴾ وقوله: (كان الله ولم يكن شيء غيره) وكذلك يحكم بحدوثها عقلا، لأن العقل يحكم ببطلان الشريك، ولو لم تكن حادثة لشاركت الله تعالى في قدمه إذن فالعالم بجميع أنواعه من أعراضه وأجرامه وعقوله ومجرداته على القول بها كلها حادثة، وهذا كلام ظاهر لا غبار عليه. هذا يدل على أن الخالق جل جلاله قد خصص مثلا عن مثل هذا بأنه علوي والآخر سفلي. إلخ . فتعين أن يكون تعالى فاعلا بالاختيار لا بالعلة ولا بالطبيعة، لأن العلة والطبيعة يستحيل يخصصا مثلا عن مثل، مع أن الذوات متباينة في المقادير والأشكال، وفعله تعالى بالاختيار يستلزم سبق عدم العالم. قال العلامة السباعي في حاشيته على شرح الدردير: واعلم أنه اتفقت جميع الملل حتى اليهود والنصارى والمجوس على حدوث ما سوى الله تعالى، ولم يخالف فى ذلك إلا شرذمة قليلة من جهلة الفلاسفة، وتبعهم على ذلك بعض من ينسب نفسه للإسلام وليس له فيه نصيب، كابن سينا والفارابي. [سباعي، ص ٢٣٩]
This is the well‑known proof among them for the contingency of the world and its need for a Maker. And you may also deduce its contingency from the fact that it consists of different types and diverse kinds, as indicated by the verses of the Noble Qur'an. That is because some of it is celestial, some terrestrial; some luminous, some dark; some hot, some cold; some moving, some still; some subtle, some dense; some are observed to exist after non‑existence, and some are observed to cease after existence, and so on. And every type of these types includes kinds, individuals, and attributes that no one can enumerate. So this indicates that it is in need of a wise Specificator, who specified each type with certain properties, so that it is contingent after non‑existence, and that its Creator is a Free Chooser, not a cause or a nature, because the effect of a cause and the imprint of a nature do not differ — assuming that to be granted. Allah said: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and the day are signs' (Qur'an 3:190). And His saying: 'Allah existed and nothing else existed with Him' (Bukhari). And reason also judges their contingency, because reason judges the falsity of a partner; and if they were not contingent, they would share with Allah Almighty in His eternity. Thus the entire world in all its types — its accidents, bodies, intellects, and abstract entities, according to those who affirm them — is all contingent. This is clear speech with no dust upon it. This indicates that the Creator, may His majesty be exalted, specified, for example, this one as celestial and another as terrestrial, etc. So it is established that He, exalted, is an Agent by choice, not by cause or nature, because a cause and a nature cannot possibly specify one like from another, given that the essences differ in quantities and shapes. And His action by choice necessitates the prior non‑existence of the world. The scholar al-Siba'i said in his gloss on Sharh al-Dardir: 'Know that all religions — even the Jews, Christians, and Magians — agree on the contingency of everything besides Allah, and no one opposed this except a small group of ignorant philosophers, and they were followed in that by some who claim to be Muslim but have no share in it, like Ibn Sina and al-Farabi.' [Siba'i, p. 239]
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage begins by referring to the previous two arguments as the well‑known proof. Then it offers an additional, independent proof: the world's immense diversity of types (celestial/terrestrial, luminous/dark, etc.). Each of these types contains countless subtypes and attributes that no one can fully enumerate. Such variegation cannot arise from a blind nature or necessary cause, because those would produce uniform effects. Instead, it demands a wise Specificator (mukhaṣṣiṣ ḥakīm) who freely chooses to assign specific properties to each thing. That implies the world is contingent, because it is specified after not being so, and that the Creator is a Free Chooser (mukhtār). The passage then cites Qur'anic and prophetic evidence (the verse from Al 'Imran and the hadith 'Allah existed and nothing else existed with Him') and adds a rational argument: reason shows that polytheism is false. If the world were eternal, it would share in God's eternity, which would imply a partner — impossible. So the world is contingent. A concluding note explains that the diversity proves the Creator acts by free choice, not necessity, since cause and nature cannot differentiate identical essences. Finally, al-Siba'i's gloss reports a near‑universal consensus among all religions (Jews, Christians, Magians) on the contingency of everything besides Allah, with only a few misguided philosophers (and those who followed them among pseudo‑Muslims like Ibn Sina and al-Farabi) dissenting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The diversity in creation is just a random result of natural processes without a designer.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that such ordered diversity cannot arise from a blind cause or nature, because necessity would produce uniformity; it requires a wise Specificator.

Checkpoint
According to Dardir, why does the diversity of types in the world prove that the Creator is a free chooser (mukhtār) rather than a cause or nature?
A) Because causes and natures produce uniform effects, not diversity.
B) Because causes and natures are eternal.
C) Because the world is composed of opposites.
D) Because the Qur'an mentions diversity.

Key Takeaway
The world's intricate diversity logically demands a wise, free-choosing Creator, proving its contingency and His free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the endless variety in creation—from the stars to the cells in your body—do you truly see the hand of a wise Specificator, or do you sometimes take it for granted? Will you pause today to consciously attribute each unique thing to His free choice?
?
The proof shows that blind causes produce only uniformity. Are there areas in your life where you attribute your circumstances to 'luck' or 'nature' rather than to the Creator's wisdom? Repent and commit to seeing His specific choice in every detail of your life.
?
Every distinct type in creation testifies that the Creator acts by free will, not necessity. How does this truth affect your trust in His choices for you, especially when they differ from your own desires? Will you submit to His specification in your life today?

Rational and Scriptural Evidence for Contingency
Dardir provides scriptural and rational proofs for the world's contingency and refutes polytheism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and revealed proofs that establish the contingency of the entire world and refute polytheism.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation together prove the world is contingent and God alone is eternal.

After presenting the diversity argument, Dardir reinforces it with both scriptural and rational proofs. He cites the Qur'anic verse about signs in creation and the prophetic hadith that 'Allah existed and nothing else existed with Him.' Then he adds a rational argument: if the world were not contingent, it would share God's eternity, implying an impossible partner. This lesson examines these two lines of evidence and their conclusion that all of creation—accidents, bodies, even intellects—is contingent.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural citations
Notice the two pieces of evidence: the Qur'anic verse (3:190) and the hadith from Bukhari. Reflect on how they directly indicate contingency.
The hadith implies that everything other than Allah came into existence after non-existence.
2
Analyze the rational argument
Read Dardir's rational statement: reason judges polytheism false; if the world were eternal it would partner with God. Understand the logical inference: sharing in eternity would entail a partner, which is impossible, so the world must be contingent.
The argument is: if the world were eternal like God, it would be a partner; but partners are rationally false; therefore the world is not eternal.
3
Appreciate the comprehensive conclusion
Dardir concludes that everything—accidents, bodies, intellects, even abstract entities—is contingent. This shows the scope of the proof.
The phrase 'على القول بها' refers to those who affirm abstract entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا هو البرهان المشهور بينهم في بيان حدوث العالم وافتقاره إلى صانع. ولك أن تستدلَّ على حدوثه بكونه أنواعًا مُختلفةً وأصْنافًا مُتباينة، كما يُشير إليه آي القرآن العزيز، وذلك لأنّ بعضه عُلويّ، وبعضه سفلي، وبعضه نوراني، وبعضه ظلماني، وبعضه حار، وبعضَه بارد، وبعضه متحرّك، وبعضه ساكن، وبعضه لطيف وبعضه كثيف، وبعضه شُوهِدَ وُجوده بعد عدَمه، وبعضه شُوهِدَ عَدَمُه بعد وجوده إلى غير ذلك. وكُلُّ نَوعِ مِنْ هذه الأنواع مُشْتَمِلٌ على أصناف وأفراد وصفات، لا قدرة لأحمد على إحصائها، فدل على أنه مُفْتَقِرٌ إلى مخصص حكيم، خص كُلَّ نَوع ببعض الحجاب عليه، فيكون حادثًا بعد عدَم، وأنَّ خالقه مُختار لا عِلة ولا طبيعةً، إذ معلول العلة ومطبوع الطبيعةِ لا يختَلِفُ على فرْضِ تسليمه. قال تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الَّيلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لآيات﴾ وقوله: (كان الله ولم يكن شيء غيره) وكذلك يحكم بحدوثها عقلا، لأن العقل يحكم ببطلان الشريك، ولو لم تكن حادثة لشاركت الله تعالى في قدمه إذن فالعالم بجميع أنواعه من أعراضه وأجرامه وعقوله ومجرداته على القول بها كلها حادثة، وهذا كلام ظاهر لا غبار عليه. هذا يدل على أن الخالق جل جلاله قد خصص مثلا عن مثل هذا بأنه علوي والآخر سفلي. إلخ . فتعين أن يكون تعالى فاعلا بالاختيار لا بالعلة ولا بالطبيعة، لأن العلة والطبيعة يستحيل يخصصا مثلا عن مثل، مع أن الذوات متباينة في المقادير والأشكال، وفعله تعالى بالاختيار يستلزم سبق عدم العالم. قال العلامة السباعي في حاشيته على شرح الدردير: واعلم أنه اتفقت جميع الملل حتى اليهود والنصارى والمجوس على حدوث ما سوى الله تعالى، ولم يخالف فى ذلك إلا شرذمة قليلة من جهلة الفلاسفة، وتبعهم على ذلك بعض من ينسب نفسه للإسلام وليس له فيه نصيب، كابن سينا والفارابي. [سباعي، ص ٢٣٩]
This is the well‑known proof among them for the contingency of the world and its need for a Maker. And you may also deduce its contingency from the fact that it consists of different types and diverse kinds, as indicated by the verses of the Noble Qur'an. That is because some of it is celestial, some terrestrial; some luminous, some dark; some hot, some cold; some moving, some still; some subtle, some dense; some are observed to exist after non‑existence, and some are observed to cease after existence, and so on. And every type of these types includes kinds, individuals, and attributes that no one can enumerate. So this indicates that it is in need of a wise Specificator, who specified each type with certain properties, so that it is contingent after non‑existence, and that its Creator is a Free Chooser, not a cause or a nature, because the effect of a cause and the imprint of a nature do not differ — assuming that to be granted. Allah said: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and the day are signs' (Qur'an 3:190). And His saying: 'Allah existed and nothing else existed with Him' (Bukhari). And reason also judges their contingency, because reason judges the falsity of a partner; and if they were not contingent, they would share with Allah Almighty in His eternity. Thus the entire world in all its types — its accidents, bodies, intellects, and abstract entities, according to those who affirm them — is all contingent. This is clear speech with no dust upon it. This indicates that the Creator, may His majesty be exalted, specified, for example, this one as celestial and another as terrestrial, etc. So it is established that He, exalted, is an Agent by choice, not by cause or nature, because a cause and a nature cannot possibly specify one like from another, given that the essences differ in quantities and shapes. And His action by choice necessitates the prior non‑existence of the world. The scholar al-Siba'i said in his gloss on Sharh al-Dardir: 'Know that all religions — even the Jews, Christians, and Magians — agree on the contingency of everything besides Allah, and no one opposed this except a small group of ignorant philosophers, and they were followed in that by some who claim to be Muslim but have no share in it, like Ibn Sina and al-Farabi.' [Siba'i, p. 239]
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage begins by referring to the previous two arguments as the well‑known proof. Then it offers an additional, independent proof: the world's immense diversity of types (celestial/terrestrial, luminous/dark, etc.). Each of these types contains countless subtypes and attributes that no one can fully enumerate. Such variegation cannot arise from a blind nature or necessary cause, because those would produce uniform effects. Instead, it demands a wise Specificator (mukhaṣṣiṣ ḥakīm) who freely chooses to assign specific properties to each thing. That implies the world is contingent, because it is specified after not being so, and that the Creator is a Free Chooser (mukhtār). The passage then cites Qur'anic and prophetic evidence (the verse from Al 'Imran and the hadith 'Allah existed and nothing else existed with Him') and adds a rational argument: reason shows that polytheism is false. If the world were eternal, it would share in God's eternity, which would imply a partner — impossible. So the world is contingent. A concluding note explains that the diversity proves the Creator acts by free choice, not necessity, since cause and nature cannot differentiate identical essences. Finally, al-Siba'i's gloss reports a near‑universal consensus among all religions (Jews, Christians, Magians) on the contingency of everything besides Allah, with only a few misguided philosophers (and those who followed them among pseudo‑Muslims like Ibn Sina and al-Farabi) dissenting.

Checkpoint
What is the rational argument Dardir gives for the world's contingency?
A) The world changes, so it must be contingent.
B) If the world were eternal, it would be a partner with God, which is rationally false.
C) The Qur'an says the world is created.
D) All philosophers agree it is contingent.

Key Takeaway
Both revelation and reason converge to prove that everything in existence besides Allah is contingent and originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
هل تعامل أي شيء في حياتك – كالوظيفة، العلاقات، أو ذكائك – وكأنه أبدي لا يزول؟ كيف يكشف لك الدرس أن كل ذلك حادث ومحتاج لله، وماذا ستفعل لتغيير هذا التعلق؟
?
عندما تتأمل آيات الله في الكون (كالسماء والأرض وتعاقب الليل والنهار)، هل تشعر حقًا بأنك حادث مفتقر إليه كل لحظة، أم تمر عليها كعادة؟ ما الذي ستفعله اليوم لتجعل هذه الآيات توقظ يقينك؟
?
الدليل العقلي يثبت استحالة وجود شريك لله. ولكن هل هناك 'شركاء' في قلبك – كالخوف من الناس، أو الرغبة في المال، أو الاعتماد على نفسك – تعاملهم كأنهم مستقلون عن الله؟ كيف ستبدأ بقطع هذا التعلق اليوم؟

Consensus on Contingency Across Religions
Al-Siba'i reports consensus of religions on contingency and identifies dissenters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the near-universal consensus among religions on the contingency of everything besides Allah, and the minority opposition from certain philosophers.

Core Idea
All major religions agree: everything besides God is contingent.

In the final part of this passage, al-Siba'i's gloss reports a remarkable fact: all religious traditions—Judaism, Christianity, Zoroastrianism—unanimously affirm that everything besides Allah is contingent. The only dissenters are a handful of misguided philosophers, including some who claim Islam but follow the likes of Ibn Sina and al-Farabi. This consensus reinforces the theological argument and highlights the deviation of those who deny contingency.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus claim
Pay attention to al-Siba'i's statement that all religions (including Jews, Christians, Magians) agree on the contingency of everything besides Allah.
This is a claim of historical consensus, not a rational argument.
2
Identify the dissenters
Note the small group that opposes: ignorant philosophers (jahalat al-falasifah) and those who follow them among pseudo-Muslims like Ibn Sina and al-Farabi.
The point is that opposition is negligible and from outside mainstream religious tradition.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this consensus bolsters the argument: if all religions agree, the doctrine of contingency is universally accepted, and dissent is an outlier.
This is used to strengthen the case for the necessity of belief in contingency.

Misconception & Correction

?

The Proof of Creation from Diversity
Imam al-Dardīr presents the proof from diversity, citing Quranic verses and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the well-known proof of the world's creation based on the diversity of its types and how it leads to affirming a free Creator.

Core Idea
Diversity in creation demands a wise, free assigner, not blind nature.

In this passage, Imam al-Dardīr presents one of the most celebrated arguments for the world's contingency—the proof from diversity. By observing the endless variety and opposing qualities in the universe, we infer the need for a Creator who chooses and specifies. This lesson unpacks that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening of the proof
Read the first sentence where al-Dardīr states that this is the well-known proof for the creation of the world and its need for a Maker.
Notice the phrase 'هذا هو البرهان المشهور'.
2
Examine the enumerated opposites
List the pairs of opposites mentioned in the passage (e.g., celestial/terrestrial, luminous/dark, hot/cold, moving/stationary, subtle/dense, existence after non-existence, ceasing after existence).
These pairs illustrate the diversity in creation.
3
Understand the inference
Al-Dardīr argues that such varied types, each with countless attributes, cannot arise from a blind cause or nature; they require a wise assigner (mukhaṣṣiṣ) who specifies each thing. This shows the world is created and the Creator acts by choice.
The key term here is 'mukhaṣṣiṣ' (assigner).
4
Review the scriptural and rational supports
The passage quotes Quranic verses and a hadith, and adds a rational argument: if the world were not created, it would share in God's eternity, which would imply a partner—impossible by reason.
The rational argument is concise but powerful.
5
Recognize the consensus
Al-Sibāʿī notes that all religious communities agree on the creation of everything other than God, except for a few misguided philosophers.
This consensus strengthens the proof.

هذا هو البرهان المشهور بينهم في بيان حدوث العالم وافتقاره إلى صانع. ولك أن تستدلَّ على حدوثه بكونه أنواعًا مُختلفةً وأصْنافًا مُتباينة، كما يُشير إليه آي القرآن العزيز، وذلك لأنّ بعضه عُلويّ، وبعضه سفلي، وبعضه نوراني، وبعضه ظلماني، وبعضه حار، وبعضَه بارد، وبعضه متحرّك، وبعضه ساكن، وبعضه لطيف وبعضه كثيف، وبعضه شُوهِدَ وُجوده بعد عدَمه ، وبعضه شُوهِدَ عَدَمُه بعد وجوده إلى غير ذلك. وكُلُّ نَوعِ مِنْ هذه الأنواع مُشْتَمِلٌ على أصناف وأفراد وصفات، لا قدرة لأحمد على إحصائها، فدل على أنه مُفْتَقِرٌ إلى مخصص حكيم، خص كُلَّ نَوع ببعض الحجاب عليه، فيكون حادثًا بعد عدَم ، وأنَّ خالقه مُختار لا عِلة ولا طبيعةً، إذ معلول المـ ومطبوع الطبيعةِ لا يختَلِفُ على فرْضِ تسليمه (۱). و قال تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الَّيلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لآيات وقوله : ( كان الله ولم يكن شيء غيره) [صحيح البخاري، كتاب بدء الخلق، باب ماجاء في قول الله تعالى وهو الذي يبدأ الخلق ثم يعيده ] وكذلك يحكم بحدوثها عقلا، لأن العقل يحكم ببطلان الشريك، ولو لم تكن حادثة لشاركت الله تعالى في قدمه إذن فالعالم بجميع أنواعه من أعراضه وأجرامه وعقوله ومجرداته على القول بها كلها حادثة، وهذا كلام ظاهر لا غبار عليه. (۱) هذا يدل على أن الخالق جل جلاله قد خصص مثلا عن مثل هذا بأنه علوي والآخر سفلي. إلخ . فتعين أن يكون تعالى فاعلا بالاختيار لا بالعلة ولا بالطبيعة، لأن العلة والطبيعة يستحيل يخصصا مثلا عن مثل، مع أن الذوات متباينة في المقادير والأشكال، وفعله تعالى بالاختيار يستلزم سبق عدم العالم. 11 قال العلامة السباعي في حاشيته على شرح الدردير واعلم أنه اتفقت جميع الملل حتى اليهود والنصارى والمجوس على حدوث ما سوى الله تعالى، ولم يخالف فى ذلك إلا شرذمة قليلة من جهلة الفلاسفة، وتبعهم على ذلك بعض من ينسب نفسه للإسلام وليس له فيه نصيب كابن سينا والفارابي. [سباعي، ص ٢٣٩]
This is the well-known proof among them for explaining the creation of the world and its need for a Maker. You may also infer its creation from the fact that it consists of different types and diverse kinds, as indicated by the verses of the noble Qur'an. This is because some of it is celestial, some terrestrial, some luminous, some dark, some hot, some cold, some moving, some stationary, some subtle, some dense, some are observed existing after non-existence, and some are observed ceasing after existence, and so on. And every kind of these types includes categories, individuals, and attributes that no one has the power to count. This indicates that it is in need of a wise assigner (mukhaṣṣiṣ) who specified each kind with some of its characteristics, so it is originated after non-existence, and that its Creator is free (mukhtār), not a cause or a nature, for the effect of a cause and the impress of nature does not differ, assuming its acceptance. And He said, the Most High: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and day are signs...' And His saying: 'Allah existed and nothing else existed with Him' [Sahih al-Bukhari]. Likewise, reason judges their creation because reason judges the falsity of a partner; if they were not created, they would share with Allah in His eternity. So the world in all its types—its accidents, bodies, intellects, and abstract entities according to those who affirm them—all are created. This is clear speech with no dust upon it. (1) This indicates that the Creator, glorified be He, specified, for example, one like this as celestial and another as terrestrial, etc. So it is established that He, the Most High, is a free agent (fāʿil bi-l-ikhtiyār), not by cause nor by nature, because cause and nature cannot possibly specify one like this over another, while essences are different in quantities and forms. And His action by choice necessitates the precedence of the world's non-existence. 11 Al-ʿAllāma al-Sibāʿī said in his gloss on Sharḥ al-Dardīr: Know that all religious communities—even the Jews, Christians, and Magians—have agreed upon the creation of everything other than Allah. None opposed that except a small group of ignorant philosophers, and they were followed by some who claim to belong to Islam but have no share in it, like Ibn Sīnā and al-Fārābī. [Sibāʿī, p. 239]
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents the well-known proof (burhān) for the creation (ḥudūth) of the world and its need for a Creator. The author begins by stating that this is the famous proof used by scholars. He then explains that one can infer the world's creation from its diverse types and contrasting kinds, as indicated by Quranic verses. The proof enumerates several pairs of opposites found in the world: celestial vs. terrestrial, luminous vs. dark, hot vs. cold, moving vs. stationary, subtle vs. dense, and that some things are observed coming into existence after non-existence, while others cease to exist after having existed. This diversity is endless. Each type contains countless categories, individuals, and attributes that no person can enumerate. This multiplicity and variation demonstrate that the world depends on a wise assigner (mukhaṣṣiṣ) who designated each kind with its particular characteristics. Consequently, the world must be originated (ḥādith) after non-existence, and its Creator must be a free agent (mukhtār), not acting by a blind cause or nature, because the effect of a cause and the imprint of nature are uniform and do not produce such varied specifications. The author then cites Quranic verses and a prophetic hadith as scriptural support, and adds a rational argument: reason judges that a partner of God is impossible; if the world were not created, it would share in God's eternity, which is false. Thus, the entire world—its accidents, bodies, intellects, and even abstract entities for those who affirm them—are all created. This is clear and undeniable. A marginal note clarifies that the diversity in the world necessitates that the Creator acts by choice, not by cause or nature, as these cannot produce such specific differentiations. Finally, the passage quotes al-Sibāʿī, who notes that all religious communities agree on the creation of everything other than God, except for a few ignorant philosophers like Ibn Sīnā and al-Fārābī, who follow them without any basis in Islam.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that diversity alone proves creation; rather, it is the specific differentiation that requires a wise, free agent.
Correction: The proof relies on the endless variety requiring a specific determiner (mukhaṣṣiṣ), not just any creator.

Checkpoint

A) The world is one uniform substance.
B) The world's varied types need a specific determiner (mukhaṣṣiṣ).
C) The world is eternal because it has always existed.
D) Philosophers proved the world's creation.

Key Takeaway
The endless diversity in the world requires a wise Creator who chooses freely, proving the world is created and not eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look at the diversity in your own life—your personality, circumstances, talents, and trials. Do you genuinely see each as a purposeful assignment from a wise Creator, or do you sometimes attribute them to random nature or luck? How would your daily gratitude change if you truly believed every detail was specifically chosen for you? Make a list this week of three specific aspects of your life that you usually take for granted, and consciously say 'Allah assigned this for me' each day.
?
The author argues that blind nature cannot produce the precise distinctions we see. Where in your life have you acted as if things 'just happen' or are 'natural'—your health, your provisions, your relationships? How does this proof call you to stop attributing outcomes to impersonal forces and instead see the hand of a free, wise Creator? Identify one area where you tend to neglect thanking Allah and commit to a specific dhikr for it.
?
If the world is entirely dependent on Allah's free choice for its very existence and specific details, what does that mean for your sense of control? Are there aspects of your life where you resist submitting to His assignment, feeling you know better? The proof demands that all diversity—even the ones you dislike—is from His wisdom. Can you trust that His assignment for you is better than your own? This week, when you face something you didn't choose, pause and say, 'My Lord, You have specified this for me, and I accept it from You.'

Defining Huduth and Qidam: The Foundation of Kalam
Dardeer defines huduth and qidam and refutes the philosophers' view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise theological definitions of huduth (origination) and qidam (eternity), and why the philosophers' alternative usage of huduth is categorically rejected in Sunni Islam.

Core Idea
Huduth means existence after non-existence; qidam means no beginning — and no middle ground exists.

In this lesson, Imam Dardeer introduces two of the most foundational concepts in Islamic theology: huduth and qidam. These terms are not just abstract definitions; they directly determine how we understand the relationship between the Creator and creation. Dardeer also addresses a major theological error: the philosophers' redefinition of huduth as mere dependence on another, which he refutes as a matter of consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Allow the verse and commentary to establish the terms before analysis.
Notice that the passage begins with a poetic line that encapsulates the definitions.
2
Define huduth and qidam
Identify the explicit definitions: huduth is existence after non-existence; qidam is the negation of a beginning of existence. Note that these are opposites with no intermediate.
3
Contrast the philosophers' view
Observe how the philosophers are mentioned: they claimed the world is eternal but still used the term huduth for other things, meaning need of another. Understand that this is not the Islamic definition.
Imam Dardeer clearly states that this belief constitutes disbelief by consensus.
4
Reflect on the exclusivity of qidam
Understand that qidam is exclusive to Allah alone. There is no third category between huduth and qidam—everything is either originated or eternal.
This dichotomy is fundamental to tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حُدوثُهُ: وُجوده بعْدَ العَدَمُ * وضده هو المُسَمّى بالقِدَمُ
(حدوثُهُ وُجوده بعد العدَم) يعني: أنَّ حدوث العالَم عِبارَةٌ عَنْ وُجودِه بعد عدمه، خلافا للفلاسفة، فإنهم ذهبوا إلى قدمه، ومع ذلك أطلقوا القَولَ بحدوث ما سوى الله تعالى، لكن بمعنى الاحتياج إلى الغَيرِ، لا بمعنى سبق العدم عليه، ومُعتقد ذلك كافر بإجماع المسلمين.
(وضدُّه) أي: ضِدُّ الحدوثِ، أي: مُقابِلُه، يعني عدَمَ أوليّةِ الوُجودِ (هو المُسَمّى بالقدم) ولا يكونُ إلا الله وحده كما سيأتي، ولا واسطة بَينَ الحدوثِ والقِدَمِ.
‘His origination: his existence after non-existence, and its opposite is called eternity.’ (Meaning that the origination of the world is an expression of its existence after its non-existence, contrary to the philosophers, for they held its eternity, yet they used the term ‘origination’ for what is other than Allah, but in the sense of need of another, not in the sense of precedence of non-existence. And whoever believes that is a disbeliever by consensus of the Muslims.) (And its opposite) i.e., the opposite of origination, i.e., its counterpart, meaning the non-primordiality of existence (is called eternity), and it is not except for Allah alone as will come, and there is no intermediate between origination and eternity.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a definition and clarification of the terms 'huduth' (origination) and 'qidam' (eternity) as used in kalam. Dardeer begins by quoting the author's verse: 'His origination: his existence after non-existence, and its opposite is called eternity.' He then explains that the origination of the world means its existence after non-existence. This is the standard position of Muslim theologians, and it is contrasted with the philosophers who claim the world is eternal. However, Dardeer notes that the philosophers still use the term 'origination' for everything other than Allah, but they mean something different: not that the thing was preceded by non-existence, but that it is in need of a cause (al-iftiqar ila al-ghayr). Dardeer then states that holding the philosophers' view constitutes disbelief by consensus of the Muslims. Next, he explains that the opposite of huduth is qidam, which is the negation of having a beginning of existence. Qidam belongs exclusively to Allah alone, and there is no intermediate state between huduth and qidam—everything is either originated or eternal.

Key Terms
حدوث
قدم
فلاسفة
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the philosophers' use of 'huduth' is acceptable or the same as the theological definition, since they still call the world 'originated' in some sense.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the philosophers' 'huduth' means ontological dependence, not temporal origination, and that this belief is categorically disbelief by consensus of Muslims.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct meaning of 'huduth' in the context of the world?
A) Existence after non-existence
B) Need of another (al-iftiqar ila al-ghayr)
C) Eternal existence
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
Huduth is existence after non-existence; qidam is the absence of a beginning — only Allah is qadim, and there is no middle ground.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself attributing some form of eternity or self-sufficiency to anything besides Allah—like your health, wealth, or relationships? How does this lesson challenge you to repent and realign your heart?
?
The philosophers used the term 'huduth' differently to avoid admitting the world was created in time. Are you ever tempted to reinterpret clear Quranic teachings to avoid uncomfortable truths? What would it cost you to accept Allah's word as it is?
?
The lesson says there is no intermediate between huduth and qidam. Everything is either created or eternal. Does your daily life reflect that only Allah is eternal and everything else is transient? Name one attachment you hold onto as if it were permanent and commit to letting go today.

The Proof from Effect to Effecter
Dardeer presents the proof for Allah's existence from the existence of the world as an effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for Allah's existence from the existence of the world as an effect, based on the principle that every effect requires an effecter.

Core Idea
The world is an effect; every effect needs a cause; therefore, Allah exists.

This lesson examines a foundational proof in Islamic theology: the argument from creation (effect) to the Creator (effecter). Imam Dardeer explains that the world is a handiwork, and like any handiwork, it necessitates a maker. He warns that denying this leads to the absurdity of preponderance without a preponderator. Let's dive into the Arabic text and unpack its logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Carefully read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's flow.
Pay attention to the key terms 'athar' and 'mu'aththir'.
2
Identify key terms
Spot the terms 'athar' (effect), 'mu'aththir' (effecter), 'sun'ah' (handiwork), 'hadith' (originated), and 'tarjih bila murajjih' (preponderance without a preponderator). Understand their definitions.
These terms form the backbone of the argument.
3
Understand the logical principle
Grasp why every effect must have an effecter: otherwise, preponderance without a preponderator would be necessary, which is impossible. This is a necessary logical truth.
This principle is not probabilistic but absolute.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that through contemplation, one recognizes Allah as the Necessary of Existence, the Owner, and the Worshipped. Connect this to the proof.
The proof is not just intellectual but leads to worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم برهن على وجوده تعالى بوجود صنعته جل وعلا فقال: إذ ظاهر بأن كل أثر يهدي إلى مؤثر فاعتبر. أي: لظهور أن العالم أثر، أي: صنعة؛ لما مر من أنه حادث. وكل أثر يهدي بفتح الياء إلى مؤثر أي: يدل على صانعه، إذ لا يعقل صنعة بدون صانع، وإلا لزم الترجيح بلا مرجح وهو محال. وإذا علمت أن كل صنعة تدل على وجود صانعها فاعتبر أي: تأمل في ملكوت السموات والأرض ودقائق الحكم؛ لتعلم بذلك أنه الواجب الوجود المالك المعبود.
Then he gave a proof for His existence, may He be exalted, by the existence of His handiwork, may He be glorified and exalted, saying: 'Since it is apparent that every effect points to an effecter, then consider.' That is, because it is apparent that the world is an effect, i.e., a handiwork, because of what has passed that it is originated. And every effect points—with the fathah on the ya'—to an effecter, i.e., indicates its maker, for a handiwork without a maker is inconceivable; otherwise, preponderance without a preponderator would be necessary, and that is impossible. And when you know that every handiwork indicates the existence of its maker, then consider, i.e., contemplate the kingdom of the heavens and the earth and the subtle points of wisdom, so that by that you may know that He is the Necessary of Existence, the Owner, the Worshipped.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the existence of Allah based on the existence of His handiwork (the created world). The author explains the line of the poem: 'Since it is apparent that every effect points to an effecter, then consider.' He clarifies that 'effect' (athar) refers to the world, which is a handiwork (sun'ah) because it is originated (hadith), as established earlier. Every effect points to an effecter (mu'aththir), meaning it indicates its maker; it is inconceivable to have a handiwork without a maker, because that would entail preponderance without a preponderator (tarjih bila murajjih), which is impossible. The author then exhorts the reader to contemplate the heavens, the earth, and the subtle wisdom within creation, so that one may come to know that Allah is the Necessary of Existence, the Owner, and the One worthy of worship. The argument follows a simple cause-and-effect logic: the world is an effect, therefore it must have an efficient cause, which is Allah.

Key Terms
أثر
مؤثر
صنعة
حادث
ترجيح بلا مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the proof is merely a probabilistic argument.
Correction: It is actually a necessary logical proof based on the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator.

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence if we deny that every effect has an effecter, according to this passage?
A) It would imply that the world has no cause.
B) It would lead to the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator.
C) It would require an infinite regress of causes.
D) It would mean the world is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The existence of the world as an effect necessitates the existence of Allah as its Creator, otherwise an absurdity (preponderance without a preponderator) would follow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the world around you, do you truly see it as an effect pointing to its Creator, or do you often forget and live as if it came from nothing? What would change in your daily life if you constantly remembered that everything you see is a sign of Allah's existence?
?
The proof says it is inconceivable to have an effect without a cause. Yet in your life, do you ever act as though your actions have no consequences, or as if the blessings you enjoy have no Giver? How can you train yourself to see the effecter behind every effect?
?
This lesson calls you to contemplate the heavens and the earth to know Allah. When was the last time you sincerely reflected on creation with the intention of increasing your certainty in Allah? What stops you from doing that today?

The Proof from Design: Every Effect Points to Its Cause
Dardeer proves God's existence by arguing that every effect points to its cause, then elaborates on creation as a sign.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument from design that demonstrates God's existence through the principle of causality and the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator.

Core Idea
Every product requires a maker, or else irrational preponderance follows.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer presents a foundational argument for God's existence based on the observed order of the universe. He begins with a concise poetic statement that every effect indicates its cause, then unpacks its logical necessity. As you read, notice how the argument moves from a general principle to a specific application to the world, and how it leads to a profound invitation to contemplate creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening poetic line
Start by reading the first line of Arabic poetry: 'Since it is apparent that every effect guides to an effective cause.' This encapsulates the entire proof.
Notice the connection between 'effect' (athar) and 'cause' (mu'aththir).
2
Understand the key terms
Identify the terms: 'athar' (effect) refers to the world as a product (sun'a), and 'mu'aththir' (effective cause) is its Creator. The world is originated (hadith), thus an effect.
The proof relies on the concept of 'tarjih bila murajjih' (preponderance without a preponderator) which is impossible.
3
Trace the logical implications
The author argues that if a product could exist without a maker, it would lead to preponderance without a preponderator, which is absurd. This is a rational necessity.
The absurdity is explained in the footnote: it combines equality and preponderance.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Once you accept the proof, you are invited to reflect on the heavens and earth to recognize God as the Necessary Existent and to grow in love and gratitude.
This reflection is not just intellectual but leads to spiritual proximity (qurb).
5
Prepare for analogical reasoning
The passage ends by signaling that examples will be given for analogical reasoning, so be ready to apply this principle to other aspects of creation.
This sets up the subsequent lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِذْ ظاهر بأنَّ كُلَّ أَثَرِ * يهدي إلى مؤَفِّرِ، فَاعْتَبر - أي: لِظُهور أنَّ العالم أثر، أي: صنعةٌ؛ لِما مرَّ مِنْ أَنه حادث. وكلُّ أَثَرِ (يَهْدي) بفَتْح الياء (إلى مؤثر) أي: يدلُّ على صانعه، إِذْ لا يُعْقَلُ صنعةٌ بدون صانع، وإلا لزم الترجيح بلا مرجح وهو محال لما من. (٢) أي ترجيح وجود العالم على عدم وجوده بلا مرجح وهو باطل لما فيه من اجتماع النقيضين المساواة والترجيح. وإذا علمتَ أنَّ كُلَّ صنعةٍ تدلّ على وُجودِ صانعها (فَاعْتَبِرِ) أَيْ: تَأَمَّلْ فِي مَلَكُوتِ السموات والأرض ودقائقِ الحِكم؛ لتَعْلَمَ بذلك أنه الواجب الوجود، المالك المعبود، القادر الودود، العلي العظيم، العليم الحكيم ، فتهتدي إلى ما خلقت لأجله، ثم تترقى إلى وفورِ حُبه وشُكْرِه، فيترتب على ذلك تفجير ينابيع الحكمة من قلبك، وتقعد في مقعد صدق عند ربك. (۱) أي عيون الحكم، والمراد العلوم والمعارف. (۲) المراد عندية مكانة لا مكان، وهي القرب المعنوي. ولنذكر لك شَيْئًا مِنْ ذلك لتقيسَ عَلَيه غَيْرَه فنقول:
Since it is apparent that every effect (athar) guides to an effective cause (mu'aththir), so reflect. That is, because it is apparent that the world is an effect, i.e., a product (sun'a), because it is established that it is originated (hadith). And every effect guides (yadullu) to its maker, since a product is inconceivable without a maker, otherwise there would be a preponderance without a preponderator (tarjih bila murajjih), which is impossible for the reason given. (2) That is, the preponderance of the existence of the world over its non-existence without a preponderator, which is false because it involves the combination of opposites: equality and preponderance. And if you know that every product indicates the existence of its maker, then reflect, i.e., contemplate the kingdom of the heavens and the earth and the subtleties of wisdom, so that you may know by that that He is the Necessary Existent, the Possessor, the Worshipped, the Powerful, the Loving, the High, the Great, the Knowing, the Wise. Then you will be guided to what you were created for, then ascend to the abundance of His love and gratitude, leading to the gushing forth of the springs of wisdom from your heart, and you will settle in a seat of truth with your Lord. (1) That is, the springs of wisdom, meaning knowledge and cognitions. (2) The meaning is a position of station (indiyya) not place, which is spiritual proximity. And we will mention for you something of that so that you may analogize from it to other things, saying:
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for God's existence from the design of the universe. It begins with a poetic line stating that every effect (athar) points to its cause. The author explains that 'effect' here refers to the world, which is a product (sun'a) because it is originated (hadith). Every product requires a maker; otherwise, the preponderance of the world's existence over non-existence would occur without a preponderator (tarjih bila murajjih), which is absurd. A footnote clarifies that this would involve a contradiction between equality and preponderance. The author then invites the reader to contemplate the heavens, earth, and subtle wisdom to recognize God as the Necessary Existent (al-wajib al-wujud) and other attributes. This contemplation leads to guidance, love, gratitude, and spiritual proximity to God. The passage ends with a transition to providing specific examples for analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Key Terms
الأثر
المؤثر
الصنعة
الترجيح بلا مرجح
الواجب الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof from design is merely empirical and probabilistic.
Correction: This proof is based on rational necessity: a product cannot exist without a maker, otherwise preponderance without a preponderator would occur, which is logically impossible.

Checkpoint
What would be the absurd consequence if a product could exist without a maker?
A) The world would be eternal.
B) Preponderance without a preponderator would occur.
C) God would be unjust.
D) The world would be illusory.

Key Takeaway
The rational necessity that every effect requires a cause leads to the affirmation of God as the Creator and Necessary Existent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that every effect requires a cause. If you are an effect of a wise Creator, what does that demand from you right now? What would it mean to ignore that reality?
?
The author says contemplating the heavens and earth leads to love and gratitude. Are you actually doing that? What prevents you from reflecting deeply on creation today?
?
If you truly knew that you were created for a purpose, would you be living as you are now? What one change would prove you believe it?

The Human Body as Evidence of God's Existence and Attributes
Dardeer uses the stages of human creation to demonstrate divine power and wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the stages of human creation and the senses serve as signs pointing to the existence, power, and wisdom of Allah.

Core Idea
Your own creation proves your Maker.

This lesson invites you to reflect on the miracle of your own creation. Imam Dardeer takes you through the stages from conception to the formation of senses and organs, showing how each step reveals divine design. He then connects this to the philosophical proof of origination (huduth).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the Qur'anic verse at the beginning and the detailed description of embryonic stages and senses.
The passage includes a footnote that explains the logical inference.
2
Identify the stages of creation
Look for the sequence: nutfa (drop) → alaqa (clot) → mudgha (lump) → formed into a beautiful shape. Also note the specific senses and organs mentioned.
These stages are presented as signs of divine craftsmanship.
3
Trace the argument from design
The passage ends with a logical conclusion: the changing and variable nature of the body's parts indicates origination (huduth) and the necessity of a wise, all-knowing, powerful Maker.
This connects the physical observation to Islamic theological proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال اللَّهُ تعالى: ﴿وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ﴾ فأنت إذا نظَرتَ إلى مبدأ خلقك وجدتَ ربَّكَ سُبحانه وتعالى قادَ والدَيكَ بِزِمامِ الشَّهْوَةِ مَقْهُورَيْنِ فِي صُورَةِ مُخْتَارَيْن مع تمام البسطِ والأُنس، وفي هذا المقام أسرار عجيبةٌ يُدْرِكُها أرباب الكَشْفِ مِنْ أَهْل الله تعالى، حتى إذا حصَلَ الوقاعُ صانَكَ اللهُ في قرار مكين، فَخَلَقَ تلك النُّطْفَةَ عَلَقَةً ثُمَّ خَلَقَ العَلَقَةَ مُضْغَةً، ثُمَّ مدَّها وصوَّرَها في أحسَنِ صُورةٍ، فجَعلَ الرأْسَ في أَحسَن خلقة، وخلَقَ العَينَ والأذن والأنف، وصوَّرَ الوَجهَ في أحسَن صورة، وأودعها مِنَ الجمال والكمال ما لا يخفى، ثُمَّ أودَعَ البصَرَ في العَينِ، والسَّمْعَ فِي الأَذُنِ، والشمَّ في الأنف، وخلَقَ الفم وزيَّنه بالشَّفَتَين، وخلَقَ اللَّسانَ وخَلَقَ فيه الذوق، وجعَلَه جُندًا مِنْ جُنودِه تعالى يُتَرْجِمُ عما في الفؤادِ مِنَ العُلوم والمعارف، وجَعَلَ الرقبة حاملة لعَرْشِ الرأْسِ فِي حُسْنِ بديع، وجعلَ فيها المنفذَ الموصلَ للأكْلِ والشُّربِ إلى المعدة وأودَعَ البَطْنَ مِنَ الأمْعاء والمصارين والقلب والكَبِدِ وغَيرها مما لا يَعْلَمُ حقيقته إلا (٤) أي وجودك بعد عدمك، يعني أن أقرب الأشياء أن ينظر المكلف فى أحواله فيستدل بها على وجوب صانعه وصفاته، فإن ذات الناظر مشتملة على سمع وبصر وكلام وذوق وشم ولمس وطول وعرض ... وكلها متبدلة متغيرة وخارجة من العدم إلى الوجود ومن الوجود إلى العدم وذلك دليل الحدوث والافتقار إلى صانع حكيم واجب الوجود عام العلم تام القدرة والإرادة
Allah the Exalted said: {And in yourselves, do you not see?} When you look at the beginning of your creation, you find your Lord, glorified and exalted, driving your parents by the rein of desire, overpowered in the form of choosers, with complete ease and intimacy. In this station are wondrous secrets perceived by the people of unveiling from among the people of Allah, until when intercourse occurs, Allah protects you in a firm resting place. Then He created that drop (nutfa) as a clot (alaqa), then created the clot as a lump (mudgha), then extended it and formed it in the best form. He made the head in the best creation, created the eye, ear, and nose, formed the face in the best form, and placed in them of beauty and perfection what is not hidden. Then He placed sight in the eye, hearing in the ear, smell in the nose, created the mouth and adorned it with lips, created the tongue and placed in it taste, and made it a soldier among His soldiers translating what is in the heart of sciences and cognitions. He made the neck carrying the throne of the head in beautiful wonder, and made in it the passage connecting eating and drinking to the stomach, and placed in the belly intestines, bowels, heart, liver, and other things whose reality none knows except (4) That is, your existence after your non-existence, meaning that the closest of things is that the responsible person looks at his own states and uses them to infer the necessity of his Maker and His attributes. For the essence of the observer includes hearing, sight, speech, taste, smell, touch, length, width... all of which are changing, variable, emerging from non-existence to existence and from existence to non-existence. That is evidence of origination (huduth) and need for a wise Maker, necessary of existence, all-encompassing in knowledge, perfect in power and will.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is an extended proof from the design of the human body. It begins by citing the Qur'anic verse 'And in yourselves, do you not see?' Then it describes the process of human creation: the parents are driven by desire, the embryo is protected in the womb, and the stages of development from nutfa to alaqa to mudgha are detailed. The formation of the head, face, senses (sight, hearing, smell, taste), and internal organs (stomach, intestines, heart, liver) are highlighted as signs of divine craftsmanship. The footnote adds that this existence after non-existence demonstrates the need for a Creator. The observer's own body, with its changing senses and dimensions, indicates origination (huduth) and dependence on a wise, powerful, and all-knowing Maker.

النطفة
العلقة
المضغة
الحواس
الحدوث
الصانع الحكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think this is merely a biological description, but the author uses it to prove the necessity of a Creator and His attributes.
Correction: The passage explicitly concludes that the changing nature of the body is evidence of origination and need for a wise Maker, not just a description of development.

Checkpoint

B) That there is no need for a creator.

Key Takeaway
The human body's complexity and changeability are clear signs of a wise Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage says your existence came after non-existence. You were nothing, then you were. Does this reality humble you when you feel self-sufficient? How can you make gratitude for your very existence a practical commitment starting now?

The Beginning of Creation: From Conception to Form
Dardeer describes the initial stages of human creation as evidence of divine wisdom and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the early stages of human conception and formation point to a wise and powerful Creator.

Core Idea
Every stage of your creation, from one cell to a perfect form, testifies to its Maker.

This lesson examines the very beginning of human life – from the act of conception to the formation of a beautifully shaped head and face. Dardeer, following the Quranic call to look within ourselves, invites us to see the divine wisdom and power in these early, hidden processes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and opening
Begin by reading the Quranic verse 'And in yourselves, do you not see?' and note how Dardeer uses it to introduce the reflection on creation.
The verse sets the method: inner reflection.
2
Trace the stages of early development
Follow the sequence from the drop of sperm to the clot, morsel, then to the formation of the head and face. Notice the gradual, ordered process.
3
Reflect on the attributes displayed
Identify the divine attributes implied at each stage – power to create from nothing, wisdom in forming complex structures, and mercy in protecting the embryo.
The passage highlights that the embryo is protected in the womb.
4
Consider the limits of human intervention
Recognize that you had no control or knowledge during this process – it was entirely God’s doing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القادر الودود، العلي العظيم، العليم الحكيم، فتهتدي إلى ما خلقت لأجله، ثم تترقى إلى وفورِ حُبه وشُكْرِه، فيترتب على ذلك تفجير ينابيع الحكمة من قلبك، وتقعد في مقعد صدق عند ربك. ولنذكر لك شَيْئًا مِنْ ذلك لتقيسَ عَلَيه غَيرَه فنقول: قال اللَّهُ تعالى: ﴿وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ﴾ فأنت إذا نظَرتَ إلى مبْدِئِ خلقك وجدتَ ربَّكَ سُبحانه وتعالى قادَ والدَيكَ بِزِمامِ الشَّهْوَةِ مَقْهُورَيْنِ فِي صورَةِ مُخْتَارَيْن مع تمام البشطِ والأُنس، وفي هذا المقام أسرار عجيبةٌ يُدْرِكُها أرباب الكَشْفِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الله تعالى، حتى إذا حصَلَ الوقاعُ صانَكَ اللهُ في قرار مكين، فَخَلَقَ تلك النُّطْفَةَ عَلَمًا خَلَقَ العَلَقَةَ مُضْعَةً، ثُمَّ مدَّها وصوَّرَها في أحسَنِ صُورةٍ، فجَعلَ الرأْسَ في أَحسَنِ خلقة، وخلَقَ العَينَ والأذن والأنف، وصوَّرَ الوَجهَ في أحسَنِ صورة، وأودعها مِنَ الجمال والكمال ما لا يخفى، ثُمَّ أودَعَ البصَرَ في العَينِ، والسَّمْعَ فِي الأَذُنِ، والشَّمَّ في الأنف، وخلَقَ الفم وزيَّنه بالشَّفَتَين، وخلَقَ اللَّسانَ وخَلَقَ فيه الذوق، وجعَلَه جُندًا مِنْ جُنودِه تعالى يُتَرْجِمُ عما في الفؤادِ مِنَ العُلوم والمعارف، وجَعَلَ الرقبة حاملة لعَرْشِ الرأْسِ فِي حُسْنٍ بديع، وجعلَ فيها المنْفَذَ المَوَصِّلَ للأكْلِ والشُّربِ إلى المعدة وأودَعَ البَطْنَ مِنَ الأمْعاء والمصارين والقلب والكَبِدِ وغَيرها مما لا يَعْلَمُ حقيقته إلا هو تعالى، وخلق الأيدي وخلق فيها الأكف والأصابع وجعَلَها مفاصل وأبدَعَها، والأرجل كذلك، وخلق العظام وكساها لحما، ثُمَّ نَفَخَ فِيكَ الرُّوحَ - وهي سر عظيمٌ عجيبٌ مِنْ أسراره تعالى - فتحَرَّكْتَ في بطنِ أُمِّكَ، وما زال بكَ رؤوفًا رَحِيمًا، حافظا لك في أضيق مكانٍ، يُوَصِّلُ لك غِذاءَكَ وأنتَ لا تَعْلَمُ شَيْئًا. حتى إذا تَمَّ خَلْقُكَ أَنزَلَكَ مِنَ الرَّحِمِ مِنْ أَضْيَقِ مَحَلٍّ فَلَطَفَ بِكَ وبأُمِّكَ، حتى إذا بَرَرْتَ أُمَّكَ بِمُجَرَّدِ النُّزولِ إِلى ثَدْيِ أُمَّكَ وأَجْرَى فِيهِ اللَّبَنَ، وَأَنزَلَ فِي قَلْبِهَا الرَّأْفَةَ والرحمة، حتى إنها ترى بَولَكَ وعَائِطَكَ مِنْ أَحْسَنِ مَا يَكونُ، والمنّةُ له تعالى في ذلك. ولما آنَ أوانُ الأكْل خَلَقَ لكَ الأسْنانَ والأضراس ورتَّبها ترتيبًا عجيبًا مع ما فيها من كمال الزينة والجمال والكمال، ثُمَّ لما قرُبَ بُلوغُكَ وكانت هذه الأسنانُ ضعيفةً أسقَطَها وأبدَلَها بأقوى منها، ثُمَّ إذا أكلتَ فَجَّرَ اللهُ فِي فَمِكَ عَيْنًا جاريةٌ – وهي الريقُ - لا ينقطعُ جريانها ما دمت تأكُلُ لتَبْتَلَّ اللَّقْمَةُ بها ويسْهُلَ بلْعُها، لا تملكها النفْسُ ولا تجري على الدوام ولا تنقطع، فانظُرْ إلى هذه الحكمة العجيبة التي أنت في غاية الافتقار إليها، وليسَ في قدرتك إجراؤها ولا منعها بالضرورة، فإذا نزَلَ الطعام والشراب في المعدة صرَّفه إلى ما يشاء، فبعضُه يتربّى به اللحم، وبعضُه يتربى به العظم، وبعضُه يتربى به الشَّحْمُ وبعضُه يتربى به الدّمُ معَ كمالِ اللَّذَّةِ حالَ الأكل وبعده، ثُمَّ ما فَضَلَ عن ذلك وكان فيه الإيذاء للبدن على تقدير إبقائه في البطن أخرَجَه مِنْ مَخْرَجَيْكَ، وانظر إلى هذين المَخْرَجَيْنِ وبديعِ حِكْمَتِهِما وإلى إقدارِكَ على إمساكهما عند تهيؤ الفَضْلَةِ للخروج. وبالجملة: فلمْ يَزَلْ سبحانَه بك رؤوفًا رحيما ودودًا كريما في كُلِّ لحظة وأنتَ غافِلٌ عَنْ نفسِكَ. وانظر إلى خروج النفس ودخوله الذي به قوامُ الرُّوحِ حالة اليقظة والنَّومِ والصَّحَةِ والمَرَضِ.
The Powerful, the Loving, the Most High, the Mighty, the All-Knowing, the Wise — so that you may be guided to what you were created for, then ascend to the abundance of His love and gratitude, resulting in the bursting forth of springs of wisdom from your heart, and you will sit in a seat of truth with your Lord. And we will mention to you something of that so that you may analogize from it to other things, and we say: Allah Most High said: 'And in yourselves, do you not see?' So when you look at the beginning of your creation, you find your Lord — glorified and exalted — leading your parents by the rein of desire, subdued in the form of free-choosers, with complete pleasure and intimacy. In this station are wondrous secrets perceived by the people of unveiling from the people of Allah Most High. When intercourse occurs, Allah protects you in a secure resting place. Then He created that sperm-drop, then created the clot, then the morsel of flesh, then extended it and formed it in the best form. He made the head in the best creation, and created the eye, ear, and nose, and shaped the face in the best form, and deposited in it beauty and perfection that is not hidden. Then He deposited sight in the eye, hearing in the ear, and smell in the nose, and created the mouth and adorned it with two lips, and created the tongue and created taste in it, and made it a soldier among His soldiers — exalted is He — translating what is in the heart of knowledge and perceptions. He made the neck a carrier of the throne of the head in beautiful innovation, and made in it the passage connecting food and drink to the stomach. And He deposited in the stomach the intestines, bowels, heart, liver, and others whose reality none knows except Him, exalted is He. And He created the hands and made in them the palms and fingers, made them joints and innovated them, and likewise the legs. He created bones and clothed them with flesh. Then He blew into you the spirit — and it is a great wondrous secret among His secrets — so you moved in your mother's womb. He remained kind and merciful to you, protecting you in the tightest place, delivering your nourishment while you knew nothing. Until when your creation was completed, He brought you down from the womb from the narrowest place, and was gentle with you and your mother. When you came out to your mother's breast, He caused milk to flow in it and placed in her heart affection and mercy, so that she considers your urine and stool as the best of things. The favor is His in that. And when the time for eating came, He created for you the teeth and molars, arranging them in a wondrous manner with the perfection of beauty, elegance, and completeness. Then when you approached maturity, and these teeth were weak, He dropped them and replaced them with stronger ones. Then when you eat, Allah causes to flow in your mouth a running spring — which is saliva — whose flow does not cease as long as you eat, to moisten the morsel and make swallowing easy. You do not control it, nor does it flow continuously, nor does it stop. So look at this wondrous wisdom to which you are in utmost need, and it is not in your power to cause it or prevent it by necessity. When food and drink descend into the stomach, He distributes them as He wills: some nourishes the flesh, some nourishes the bone, some nourishes the fat, some nourishes the blood, with complete pleasure during and after eating. Then what remains beyond that, which would harm the body if kept in the stomach, He expels from your two exits. Look at these two exits and the wondrous wisdom of them, and at how He enabled you to hold them back when the waste is ready to exit. In short, He — glorified is He — has remained kind, merciful, loving, and generous to you every moment while you are heedless of yourself. And look at the exhalation and inhalation of breath, by which the spirit is sustained, whether awake or asleep, in health or sickness.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof of God's existence, attributes, and wisdom through reflection on the stages of human creation. Dardeer begins by citing the Quranic verse "And in yourselves, do you not see?" (Quran 51:21), establishing the method of inner reflection. He then traces human development from conception to adulthood, emphasizing divine control, wisdom, and mercy at every step. The argument is teleological: each intricate detail of the body — the senses, organs, bones, skin, digestion, and even the nursing instinct — points to a wise and powerful Creator. The proof concludes with the observation that God's continuous care for humans continues every moment, even though humans are often heedless. The passage refutes atheism by showing that such complexity cannot arise by chance.

Key Terms
النطفة (nutfa - drop)
العلقة (alaqa - clot)
المضغة (mudgha - morsel of flesh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that embryonic development is a purely natural process without divine intervention at each step.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that God directly creates each stage, from the drop to the formed face, demonstrating ongoing divine action.

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, what are the three stages mentioned after the drop?
A) Drop, bone, flesh
B) Drop, clot, morsel of flesh
C) Drop, embryo, fetus
D) Drop, blood, limb

Key Takeaway
The early stages of human life, from conception to facial formation, clearly demonstrate the existence of a wise and powerful Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own beginning—your conception, your formation in the womb, the features of your face—do you truly see the hand of God in every detail, or do you take these for granted as mere biology? What would change if you saw them as direct acts of God upon you?
?
The passage says your parents were 'subdued in the form of free-choosers'—driven by desire while God led them. How does this reality challenge your illusion of total control over your own choices? Will you acknowledge that every decision you make is within God's overarching plan, and submit to His guidance?
?
Every time you look in the mirror, you see a face shaped by God in the best form, with eyes, ears, and nose perfectly placed. Are you grateful for this craftsmanship, or do you complain about its imperfections? What specific act of gratitude can you offer today for the gift of your own creation?
