The Senses, Organs, and Limbs
Dardeer describes the creation of senses, internal organs, and limbs as further evidence of divine wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the creation of the senses, internal organs, and limbs reveals God's planning and generosity.

Core Idea
Every sense, organ, and limb is a gift from God, designed with purpose and perfection.

This lesson continues the proof by examining the next phase of creation: the placement of senses in the eyes, ears, and nose, the formation of the mouth, tongue, neck, stomach with its organs, and the hands, legs, and skeleton. Each detail serves a function and shows divine design.

Guided Path
1
Identify the senses and their organs
Read about how God deposits sight in the eye, hearing in the ear, and smell in the nose. Notice the specific assignment.
The senses are not created randomly; each is placed in its appropriate organ.
2
Examine the mouth and tongue
See how the mouth is adorned with lips, and the tongue is created with taste and used as a translator of knowledge.
The tongue's function goes beyond tasting; it expresses the heart's knowledge.
3
Trace the internal organs
Follow the creation of the neck as a passage, and the stomach with its complex system of intestines, heart, liver, etc.
These are hidden from human knowledge; only God knows their true reality.
4
Consider the limbs and bones
Notice the hands, palms, fingers, joints, and legs, and how bones are clothed with flesh.
The skeletal structure provides support and movement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القادر الودود، العلي العظيم، العليم الحكيم، فتهتدي إلى ما خلقت لأجله، ثم تترقى إلى وفورِ حُبه وشُكْرِه، فيترتب على ذلك تفجير ينابيع الحكمة من قلبك، وتقعد في مقعد صدق عند ربك. ولنذكر لك شَيْئًا مِنْ ذلك لتقيسَ عَلَيه غَيرَه فنقول: قال اللَّهُ تعالى: ﴿وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ﴾ فأنت إذا نظَرتَ إلى مبْدِئِ خلقك وجدتَ ربَّكَ سُبحانه وتعالى قادَ والدَيكَ بِزِمامِ الشَّهْوَةِ مَقْهُورَيْنِ فِي صورَةِ مُخْتَارَيْن مع تمام البشطِ والأُنس، وفي هذا المقام أسرار عجيبةٌ يُدْرِكُها أرباب الكَشْفِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الله تعالى، حتى إذا حصَلَ الوقاعُ صانَكَ اللهُ في قرار مكين، فَخَلَقَ تلك النُّطْفَةَ عَلَمًا خَلَقَ العَلَقَةَ مُضْعَةً، ثُمَّ مدَّها وصوَّرَها في أحسَنِ صُورةٍ، فجَعلَ الرأْسَ في أَحسَنِ خلقة، وخلَقَ العَينَ والأذن والأنف، وصوَّرَ الوَجهَ في أحسَنِ صورة، وأودعها مِنَ الجمال والكمال ما لا يخفى، ثُمَّ أودَعَ البصَرَ في العَينِ، والسَّمْعَ فِي الأَذُنِ، والشَّمَّ في الأنف، وخلَقَ الفم وزيَّنه بالشَّفَتَين، وخلَقَ اللَّسانَ وخَلَقَ فيه الذوق، وجعَلَه جُندًا مِنْ جُنودِه تعالى يُتَرْجِمُ عما في الفؤادِ مِنَ العُلوم والمعارف، وجَعَلَ الرقبة حاملة لعَرْشِ الرأْسِ فِي حُسْنٍ بديع، وجعلَ فيها المنْفَذَ المَوَصِّلَ للأكْلِ والشُّربِ إلى المعدة وأودَعَ البَطْنَ مِنَ الأمْعاء والمصارين والقلب والكَبِدِ وغَيرها مما لا يَعْلَمُ حقيقته إلا هو تعالى، وخلق الأيدي وخلق فيها الأكف والأصابع وجعَلَها مفاصل وأبدَعَها، والأرجل كذلك، وخلق العظام وكساها لحما، ثُمَّ نَفَخَ فِيكَ الرُّوحَ - وهي سر عظيمٌ عجيبٌ مِنْ أسراره تعالى - فتحَرَّكْتَ في بطنِ أُمِّكَ، وما زال بكَ رؤوفًا رَحِيمًا، حافظا لك في أضيق مكانٍ، يُوَصِّلُ لك غِذاءَكَ وأنتَ لا تَعْلَمُ شَيْئًا. حتى إذا تَمَّ خَلْقُكَ أَنزَلَكَ مِنَ الرَّحِمِ مِنْ أَضْيَقِ مَحَلٍّ فَلَطَفَ بِكَ وبأُمِّكَ، حتى إذا بَرَرْتَ أُمَّكَ بِمُجَرَّدِ النُّزولِ إِلى ثَدْيِ أُمَّكَ وأَجْرَى فِيهِ اللَّبَنَ، وَأَنزَلَ فِي قَلْبِهَا الرَّأْفَةَ والرحمة، حتى إنها ترى بَولَكَ وعَائِطَكَ مِنْ أَحْسَنِ مَا يَكونُ، والمنّةُ له تعالى في ذلك. ولما آنَ أوانُ الأكْل خَلَقَ لكَ الأسْنانَ والأضراس ورتَّبها ترتيبًا عجيبًا مع ما فيها من كمال الزينة والجمال والكمال، ثُمَّ لما قرُبَ بُلوغُكَ وكانت هذه الأسنانُ ضعيفةً أسقَطَها وأبدَلَها بأقوى منها، ثُمَّ إذا أكلتَ فَجَّرَ اللهُ فِي فَمِكَ عَيْنًا جاريةٌ – وهي الريقُ - لا ينقطعُ جريانها ما دمت تأكُلُ لتَبْتَلَّ اللَّقْمَةُ بها ويسْهُلَ بلْعُها، لا تملكها النفْسُ ولا تجري على الدوام ولا تنقطع، فانظُرْ إلى هذه الحكمة العجيبة التي أنت في غاية الافتقار إليها، وليسَ في قدرتك إجراؤها ولا منعها بالضرورة، فإذا نزَلَ الطعام والشراب في المعدة صرَّفه إلى ما يشاء، فبعضُه يتربّى به اللحم، وبعضُه يتربى به العظم، وبعضُه يتربى به الشَّحْمُ وبعضُه يتربى به الدّمُ معَ كمالِ اللَّذَّةِ حالَ الأكل وبعده، ثُمَّ ما فَضَلَ عن ذلك وكان فيه الإيذاء للبدن على تقدير إبقائه في البطن أخرَجَه مِنْ مَخْرَجَيْكَ، وانظر إلى هذين المَخْرَجَيْنِ وبديعِ حِكْمَتِهِما وإلى إقدارِكَ على إمساكهما عند تهيؤ الفَضْلَةِ للخروج. وبالجملة: فلمْ يَزَلْ سبحانَه بك رؤوفًا رحيما ودودًا كريما في كُلِّ لحظة وأنتَ غافِلٌ عَنْ نفسِكَ. وانظر إلى خروج النفس ودخوله الذي به قوامُ الرُّوحِ حالة اليقظة والنَّومِ والصَّحَةِ والمَرَضِ.
The Powerful, the Loving, the Most High, the Mighty, the All-Knowing, the Wise — so that you may be guided to what you were created for, then ascend to the abundance of His love and gratitude, resulting in the bursting forth of springs of wisdom from your heart, and you will sit in a seat of truth with your Lord. And we will mention to you something of that so that you may analogize from it to other things, and we say: Allah Most High said: 'And in yourselves, do you not see?' So when you look at the beginning of your creation, you find your Lord — glorified and exalted — leading your parents by the rein of desire, subdued in the form of free-choosers, with complete pleasure and intimacy. In this station are wondrous secrets perceived by the people of unveiling from the people of Allah Most High. When intercourse occurs, Allah protects you in a secure resting place. Then He created that sperm-drop, then created the clot, then the morsel of flesh, then extended it and formed it in the best form. He made the head in the best creation, and created the eye, ear, and nose, and shaped the face in the best form, and deposited in it beauty and perfection that is not hidden. Then He deposited sight in the eye, hearing in the ear, and smell in the nose, and created the mouth and adorned it with two lips, and created the tongue and created taste in it, and made it a soldier among His soldiers — exalted is He — translating what is in the heart of knowledge and perceptions. He made the neck a carrier of the throne of the head in beautiful innovation, and made in it the passage connecting food and drink to the stomach. And He deposited in the stomach the intestines, bowels, heart, liver, and others whose reality none knows except Him, exalted is He. And He created the hands and made in them the palms and fingers, made them joints and innovated them, and likewise the legs. He created bones and clothed them with flesh. Then He blew into you the spirit — and it is a great wondrous secret among His secrets — so you moved in your mother's womb. He remained kind and merciful to you, protecting you in the tightest place, delivering your nourishment while you knew nothing. Until when your creation was completed, He brought you down from the womb from the narrowest place, and was gentle with you and your mother. When you came out to your mother's breast, He caused milk to flow in it and placed in her heart affection and mercy, so that she considers your urine and stool as the best of things. The favor is His in that. And when the time for eating came, He created for you the teeth and molars, arranging them in a wondrous manner with the perfection of beauty, elegance, and completeness. Then when you approached maturity, and these teeth were weak, He dropped them and replaced them with stronger ones. Then when you eat, Allah causes to flow in your mouth a running spring — which is saliva — whose flow does not cease as long as you eat, to moisten the morsel and make swallowing easy. You do not control it, nor does it flow continuously, nor does it stop. So look at this wondrous wisdom to which you are in utmost need, and it is not in your power to cause it or prevent it by necessity. When food and drink descend into the stomach, He distributes them as He wills: some nourishes the flesh, some nourishes the bone, some nourishes the fat, some nourishes the blood, with complete pleasure during and after eating. Then what remains beyond that, which would harm the body if kept in the stomach, He expels from your two exits. Look at these two exits and the wondrous wisdom of them, and at how He enabled you to hold them back when the waste is ready to exit. In short, He — glorified is He — has remained kind, merciful, loving, and generous to you every moment while you are heedless of yourself. And look at the exhalation and inhalation of breath, by which the spirit is sustained, whether awake or asleep, in health or sickness.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof of God's existence, attributes, and wisdom through reflection on the stages of human creation. Dardeer begins by citing the Quranic verse "And in yourselves, do you not see?" (Quran 51:21), establishing the method of inner reflection. He then traces human development from conception to adulthood, emphasizing divine control, wisdom, and mercy at every step. The argument is teleological: each intricate detail of the body — the senses, organs, bones, skin, digestion, and even the nursing instinct — points to a wise and powerful Creator. The proof concludes with the observation that God's continuous care for humans continues every moment, even though humans are often heedless. The passage refutes atheism by showing that such complexity cannot arise by chance.

Key Terms
البصر (basr - sight)
السمع (sam' - hearing)
الذوق (dhawq - taste)
القلب (qalb - heart)
الكبد (kabid - liver)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might assume the body’s complexity is simply a result of evolution and chance.
Correction: The passage highlights that each part is intentionally placed by God, with specific functions, and that the true reality of organs is known only to Him.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the tongue do besides tasting?
A) It helps in chewing
B) It translates what is in the heart
C) It assists in swallowing
D) It aids in breathing

Key Takeaway
The precise creation of senses, internal organs, and limbs shows God's intentional design and generosity toward humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your hand, do you see it as a mere tool or as a crafted gift from Allah, made with precision and joints? How would your daily actions change if you truly felt that each finger is a sign of His mercy?
?
You rely on your tongue every day to taste and speak. Have you ever considered that its ability to translate the knowledge in your heart is a soldier of Allah? How will you use that soldier tomorrow in a way that honors its Creator?
?
The passage says that the true reality of your heart and liver is known only to Allah. Does this humble you to admit that you do not fully understand your own body? What would it mean for you to submit to Allah's knowledge over your own?

Allah's Existence
beginner
5 min
The Spirit, Birth, and Divine Care
Dardeer describes the ensoulment, birth, and early nurturing as signs of God's mercy and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the blowing of the spirit and the process of birth demonstrate God's mercy and care.

Core Idea
From the spirit to the breast, God's kindness surrounds us before we are even aware.

This lesson covers the moment the soul is breathed into the body, causing movement in the womb, and then the gentle birth and provision of milk. It emphasizes God's protection and tenderness throughout, even for bodily functions like urine and stool.

Guided Path
1
Reflect on the blowing of the spirit
Read about how God breathes the spirit into you, causing movement in the womb. The spirit is described as a great secret.
The spirit is a divine secret, beyond full human comprehension.
2
Notice divine protection and sustenance
See how God protects you in the tightest place and provides nourishment without your knowledge.
God's care is constant and unseen.
3
Trace the birth process
Observe how you are brought out of the narrowest place with gentleness to you and your mother.
The difficulty of birth is eased by divine gentleness.
4
Appreciate the provision of milk
Understand how God places milk in the breast and puts affection in the mother's heart so she cares for you lovingly.
Even the mother's compassion is a gift from God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القادر الودود، العلي العظيم، العليم الحكيم، فتهتدي إلى ما خلقت لأجله، ثم تترقى إلى وفورِ حُبه وشُكْرِه، فيترتب على ذلك تفجير ينابيع الحكمة من قلبك، وتقعد في مقعد صدق عند ربك. ولنذكر لك شَيْئًا مِنْ ذلك لتقيسَ عَلَيه غَيرَه فنقول: قال اللَّهُ تعالى: ﴿وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ﴾ فأنت إذا نظَرتَ إلى مبْدِئِ خلقك وجدتَ ربَّكَ سُبحانه وتعالى قادَ والدَيكَ بِزِمامِ الشَّهْوَةِ مَقْهُورَيْنِ فِي صورَةِ مُخْتَارَيْن مع تمام البشطِ والأُنس، وفي هذا المقام أسرار عجيبةٌ يُدْرِكُها أرباب الكَشْفِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الله تعالى، حتى إذا حصَلَ الوقاعُ صانَكَ اللهُ في قرار مكين، فَخَلَقَ تلك النُّطْفَةَ عَلَمًا خَلَقَ العَلَقَةَ مُضْعَةً، ثُمَّ مدَّها وصوَّرَها في أحسَنِ صُورةٍ، فجَعلَ الرأْسَ في أَحسَنِ خلقة، وخلَقَ العَينَ والأذن والأنف، وصوَّرَ الوَجهَ في أحسَنِ صورة، وأودعها مِنَ الجمال والكمال ما لا يخفى، ثُمَّ أودَعَ البصَرَ في العَينِ، والسَّمْعَ فِي الأَذُنِ، والشَّمَّ في الأنف، وخلَقَ الفم وزيَّنه بالشَّفَتَين، وخلَقَ اللَّسانَ وخَلَقَ فيه الذوق، وجعَلَه جُندًا مِنْ جُنودِه تعالى يُتَرْجِمُ عما في الفؤادِ مِنَ العُلوم والمعارف، وجَعَلَ الرقبة حاملة لعَرْشِ الرأْسِ فِي حُسْنٍ بديع، وجعلَ فيها المنْفَذَ المَوَصِّلَ للأكْلِ والشُّربِ إلى المعدة وأودَعَ البَطْنَ مِنَ الأمْعاء والمصارين والقلب والكَبِدِ وغَيرها مما لا يَعْلَمُ حقيقته إلا هو تعالى، وخلق الأيدي وخلق فيها الأكف والأصابع وجعَلَها مفاصل وأبدَعَها، والأرجل كذلك، وخلق العظام وكساها لحما، ثُمَّ نَفَخَ فِيكَ الرُّوحَ - وهي سر عظيمٌ عجيبٌ مِنْ أسراره تعالى - فتحَرَّكْتَ في بطنِ أُمِّكَ، وما زال بكَ رؤوفًا رَحِيمًا، حافظا لك في أضيق مكانٍ، يُوَصِّلُ لك غِذاءَكَ وأنتَ لا تَعْلَمُ شَيْئًا. حتى إذا تَمَّ خَلْقُكَ أَنزَلَكَ مِنَ الرَّحِمِ مِنْ أَضْيَقِ مَحَلٍّ فَلَطَفَ بِكَ وبأُمِّكَ، حتى إذا بَرَرْتَ أُمَّكَ بِمُجَرَّدِ النُّزولِ إِلى ثَدْيِ أُمَّكَ وأَجْرَى فِيهِ اللَّبَنَ، وَأَنزَلَ فِي قَلْبِهَا الرَّأْفَةَ والرحمة، حتى إنها ترى بَولَكَ وعَائِطَكَ مِنْ أَحْسَنِ مَا يَكونُ، والمنّةُ له تعالى في ذلك. ولما آنَ أوانُ الأكْل خَلَقَ لكَ الأسْنانَ والأضراس ورتَّبها ترتيبًا عجيبًا مع ما فيها من كمال الزينة والجمال والكمال، ثُمَّ لما قرُبَ بُلوغُكَ وكانت هذه الأسنانُ ضعيفةً أسقَطَها وأبدَلَها بأقوى منها، ثُمَّ إذا أكلتَ فَجَّرَ اللهُ فِي فَمِكَ عَيْنًا جاريةٌ – وهي الريقُ - لا ينقطعُ جريانها ما دمت تأكُلُ لتَبْتَلَّ اللَّقْمَةُ بها ويسْهُلَ بلْعُها، لا تملكها النفْسُ ولا تجري على الدوام ولا تنقطع، فانظُرْ إلى هذه الحكمة العجيبة التي أنت في غاية الافتقار إليها، وليسَ في قدرتك إجراؤها ولا منعها بالضرورة، فإذا نزَلَ الطعام والشراب في المعدة صرَّفه إلى ما يشاء، فبعضُه يتربّى به اللحم، وبعضُه يتربى به العظم، وبعضُه يتربى به الشَّحْمُ وبعضُه يتربى به الدّمُ معَ كمالِ اللَّذَّةِ حالَ الأكل وبعده، ثُمَّ ما فَضَلَ عن ذلك وكان فيه الإيذاء للبدن على تقدير إبقائه في البطن أخرَجَه مِنْ مَخْرَجَيْكَ، وانظر إلى هذين المَخْرَجَيْنِ وبديعِ حِكْمَتِهِما وإلى إقدارِكَ على إمساكهما عند تهيؤ الفَضْلَةِ للخروج. وبالجملة: فلمْ يَزَلْ سبحانَه بك رؤوفًا رحيما ودودًا كريما في كُلِّ لحظة وأنتَ غافِلٌ عَنْ نفسِكَ. وانظر إلى خروج النفس ودخوله الذي به قوامُ الرُّوحِ حالة اليقظة والنَّومِ والصَّحَةِ والمَرَضِ.
The Powerful, the Loving, the Most High, the Mighty, the All-Knowing, the Wise — so that you may be guided to what you were created for, then ascend to the abundance of His love and gratitude, resulting in the bursting forth of springs of wisdom from your heart, and you will sit in a seat of truth with your Lord. And we will mention to you something of that so that you may analogize from it to other things, and we say: Allah Most High said: 'And in yourselves, do you not see?' So when you look at the beginning of your creation, you find your Lord — glorified and exalted — leading your parents by the rein of desire, subdued in the form of free-choosers, with complete pleasure and intimacy. In this station are wondrous secrets perceived by the people of unveiling from the people of Allah Most High. When intercourse occurs, Allah protects you in a secure resting place. Then He created that sperm-drop, then created the clot, then the morsel of flesh, then extended it and formed it in the best form. He made the head in the best creation, and created the eye, ear, and nose, and shaped the face in the best form, and deposited in it beauty and perfection that is not hidden. Then He deposited sight in the eye, hearing in the ear, and smell in the nose, and created the mouth and adorned it with two lips, and created the tongue and created taste in it, and made it a soldier among His soldiers — exalted is He — translating what is in the heart of knowledge and perceptions. He made the neck a carrier of the throne of the head in beautiful innovation, and made in it the passage connecting food and drink to the stomach. And He deposited in the stomach the intestines, bowels, heart, liver, and others whose reality none knows except Him, exalted is He. And He created the hands and made in them the palms and fingers, made them joints and innovated them, and likewise the legs. He created bones and clothed them with flesh. Then He blew into you the spirit — and it is a great wondrous secret among His secrets — so you moved in your mother's womb. He remained kind and merciful to you, protecting you in the tightest place, delivering your nourishment while you knew nothing. Until when your creation was completed, He brought you down from the womb from the narrowest place, and was gentle with you and your mother. When you came out to your mother's breast, He caused milk to flow in it and placed in her heart affection and mercy, so that she considers your urine and stool as the best of things. The favor is His in that. And when the time for eating came, He created for you the teeth and molars, arranging them in a wondrous manner with the perfection of beauty, elegance, and completeness. Then when you approached maturity, and these teeth were weak, He dropped them and replaced them with stronger ones. Then when you eat, Allah causes to flow in your mouth a running spring — which is saliva — whose flow does not cease as long as you eat, to moisten the morsel and make swallowing easy. You do not control it, nor does it flow continuously, nor does it stop. So look at this wondrous wisdom to which you are in utmost need, and it is not in your power to cause it or prevent it by necessity. When food and drink descend into the stomach, He distributes them as He wills: some nourishes the flesh, some nourishes the bone, some nourishes the fat, some nourishes the blood, with complete pleasure during and after eating. Then what remains beyond that, which would harm the body if kept in the stomach, He expels from your two exits. Look at these two exits and the wondrous wisdom of them, and at how He enabled you to hold them back when the waste is ready to exit. In short, He — glorified is He — has remained kind, merciful, loving, and generous to you every moment while you are heedless of yourself. And look at the exhalation and inhalation of breath, by which the spirit is sustained, whether awake or asleep, in health or sickness.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof of God's existence, attributes, and wisdom through reflection on the stages of human creation. Dardeer begins by citing the Quranic verse "And in yourselves, do you not see?" (Quran 51:21), establishing the method of inner reflection. He then traces human development from conception to adulthood, emphasizing divine control, wisdom, and mercy at every step. The argument is teleological: each intricate detail of the body — the senses, organs, bones, skin, digestion, and even the nursing instinct — points to a wise and powerful Creator. The proof concludes with the observation that God's continuous care for humans continues every moment, even though humans are often heedless. The passage refutes atheism by showing that such complexity cannot arise by chance.

Key Terms
الروح (ruh - spirit)
الرحمة (rahma - mercy)
الرأفة (ra'fa - affection)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a mother's love is purely natural instinct without divine origin.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that God places affection and mercy in the mother's heart, showing it is a divine gift.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens right after the baby is born?
A) The baby starts walking
B) The mother's breast produces milk and she feels affection
C) The baby is bathed
D) The father names the child

Key Takeaway
The spirit, birth, and mother's milk are all direct gifts from God, demonstrating His mercy and care from the very beginning of life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You were nourished in the womb without knowing anything. In what areas of your life might God be providing for you right now without your awareness? How can you train yourself to recognize His unseen care?
?
God placed in your mother's heart such affection that she considered your waste as 'the best of things.' Can you identify any difficult or unpleasant situation in your life that, if seen through God's mercy, could actually be a sign of His kindness? What would change if you saw it that way?
?
The spirit is called a 'great wondrous secret.' Have you ever paused to consider the mystery of your own soul—that it is directly from God? How does this realization affect your sense of purpose and accountability to Him today?

Sustenance and Wisdom in Daily Life
Dardeer concludes the proof with daily bodily functions as ongoing signs of divine wisdom and mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how everyday processes like eating, digestion, and breathing point to God's wisdom and control.

Core Idea
Even the simplest bodily functions—like chewing, digesting, and breathing—are signs of divine wisdom.

This lesson explores the later stages of human life: the replacement of teeth, the flow of saliva during eating, the distribution of food in the body, and the process of waste elimination. It concludes with a summary and reflection on breathing. All these often-overlooked processes are powerful proofs of God's wisdom and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Observe the replacement of teeth
Notice how God creates milk teeth, then replaces them with stronger adult teeth at the right time.
This shows foresight and planning.
2
Reflect on saliva during eating
Consider the flow of saliva that helps moisten food—it comes only when needed and is not under your control.
Saliva is a 'running spring' in the mouth, a graceful provision.
3
Trace the distribution of food
Understand how food is transformed into flesh, bone, fat, and blood, with pleasure during and after eating.
This distribution is beyond human power and shows divine arrangement.
4
Consider waste elimination and breath
See how waste is expelled in a balanced way, and how breathing continues night and day without thought.
These automatic processes sustain life and are signs of God's constant care.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القادر الودود، العلي العظيم، العليم الحكيم، فتهتدي إلى ما خلقت لأجله، ثم تترقى إلى وفورِ حُبه وشُكْرِه، فيترتب على ذلك تفجير ينابيع الحكمة من قلبك، وتقعد في مقعد صدق عند ربك. ولنذكر لك شَيْئًا مِنْ ذلك لتقيسَ عَلَيه غَيرَه فنقول: قال اللَّهُ تعالى: ﴿وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ﴾ فأنت إذا نظَرتَ إلى مبْدِئِ خلقك وجدتَ ربَّكَ سُبحانه وتعالى قادَ والدَيكَ بِزِمامِ الشَّهْوَةِ مَقْهُورَيْنِ فِي صورَةِ مُخْتَارَيْن مع تمام البشطِ والأُنس، وفي هذا المقام أسرار عجيبةٌ يُدْرِكُها أرباب الكَشْفِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الله تعالى، حتى إذا حصَلَ الوقاعُ صانَكَ اللهُ في قرار مكين، فَخَلَقَ تلك النُّطْفَةَ عَلَمًا خَلَقَ العَلَقَةَ مُضْعَةً، ثُمَّ مدَّها وصوَّرَها في أحسَنِ صُورةٍ، فجَعلَ الرأْسَ في أَحسَنِ خلقة، وخلَقَ العَينَ والأذن والأنف، وصوَّرَ الوَجهَ في أحسَنِ صورة، وأودعها مِنَ الجمال والكمال ما لا يخفى، ثُمَّ أودَعَ البصَرَ في العَينِ، والسَّمْعَ فِي الأَذُنِ، والشَّمَّ في الأنف، وخلَقَ الفم وزيَّنه بالشَّفَتَين، وخلَقَ اللَّسانَ وخَلَقَ فيه الذوق، وجعَلَه جُندًا مِنْ جُنودِه تعالى يُتَرْجِمُ عما في الفؤادِ مِنَ العُلوم والمعارف، وجَعَلَ الرقبة حاملة لعَرْشِ الرأْسِ فِي حُسْنٍ بديع، وجعلَ فيها المنْفَذَ المَوَصِّلَ للأكْلِ والشُّربِ إلى المعدة وأودَعَ البَطْنَ مِنَ الأمْعاء والمصارين والقلب والكَبِدِ وغَيرها مما لا يَعْلَمُ حقيقته إلا هو تعالى، وخلق الأيدي وخلق فيها الأكف والأصابع وجعَلَها مفاصل وأبدَعَها، والأرجل كذلك، وخلق العظام وكساها لحما، ثُمَّ نَفَخَ فِيكَ الرُّوحَ - وهي سر عظيمٌ عجيبٌ مِنْ أسراره تعالى - فتحَرَّكْتَ في بطنِ أُمِّكَ، وما زال بكَ رؤوفًا رَحِيمًا، حافظا لك في أضيق مكانٍ، يُوَصِّلُ لك غِذاءَكَ وأنتَ لا تَعْلَمُ شَيْئًا. حتى إذا تَمَّ خَلْقُكَ أَنزَلَكَ مِنَ الرَّحِمِ مِنْ أَضْيَقِ مَحَلٍّ فَلَطَفَ بِكَ وبأُمِّكَ، حتى إذا بَرَرْتَ أُمَّكَ بِمُجَرَّدِ النُّزولِ إِلى ثَدْيِ أُمَّكَ وأَجْرَى فِيهِ اللَّبَنَ، وَأَنزَلَ فِي قَلْبِهَا الرَّأْفَةَ والرحمة، حتى إنها ترى بَولَكَ وعَائِطَكَ مِنْ أَحْسَنِ مَا يَكونُ، والمنّةُ له تعالى في ذلك. ولما آنَ أوانُ الأكْل خَلَقَ لكَ الأسْنانَ والأضراس ورتَّبها ترتيبًا عجيبًا مع ما فيها من كمال الزينة والجمال والكمال، ثُمَّ لما قرُبَ بُلوغُكَ وكانت هذه الأسنانُ ضعيفةً أسقَطَها وأبدَلَها بأقوى منها، ثُمَّ إذا أكلتَ فَجَّرَ اللهُ فِي فَمِكَ عَيْنًا جاريةٌ – وهي الريقُ - لا ينقطعُ جريانها ما دمت تأكُلُ لتَبْتَلَّ اللَّقْمَةُ بها ويسْهُلَ بلْعُها، لا تملكها النفْسُ ولا تجري على الدوام ولا تنقطع، فانظُرْ إلى هذه الحكمة العجيبة التي أنت في غاية الافتقار إليها، وليسَ في قدرتك إجراؤها ولا منعها بالضرورة، فإذا نزَلَ الطعام والشراب في المعدة صرَّفه إلى ما يشاء، فبعضُه يتربّى به اللحم، وبعضُه يتربى به العظم، وبعضُه يتربى به الشَّحْمُ وبعضُه يتربى به الدّمُ معَ كمالِ اللَّذَّةِ حالَ الأكل وبعده، ثُمَّ ما فَضَلَ عن ذلك وكان فيه الإيذاء للبدن على تقدير إبقائه في البطن أخرَجَه مِنْ مَخْرَجَيْكَ، وانظر إلى هذين المَخْرَجَيْنِ وبديعِ حِكْمَتِهِما وإلى إقدارِكَ على إمساكهما عند تهيؤ الفَضْلَةِ للخروج. وبالجملة: فلمْ يَزَلْ سبحانَه بك رؤوفًا رحيما ودودًا كريما في كُلِّ لحظة وأنتَ غافِلٌ عَنْ نفسِكَ. وانظر إلى خروج النفس ودخوله الذي به قوامُ الرُّوحِ حالة اليقظة والنَّومِ والصَّحَةِ والمَرَضِ.
The Powerful, the Loving, the Most High, the Mighty, the All-Knowing, the Wise — so that you may be guided to what you were created for, then ascend to the abundance of His love and gratitude, resulting in the bursting forth of springs of wisdom from your heart, and you will sit in a seat of truth with your Lord. And we will mention to you something of that so that you may analogize from it to other things, and we say: Allah Most High said: 'And in yourselves, do you not see?' So when you look at the beginning of your creation, you find your Lord — glorified and exalted — leading your parents by the rein of desire, subdued in the form of free-choosers, with complete pleasure and intimacy. In this station are wondrous secrets perceived by the people of unveiling from the people of Allah Most High. When intercourse occurs, Allah protects you in a secure resting place. Then He created that sperm-drop, then created the clot, then the morsel of flesh, then extended it and formed it in the best form. He made the head in the best creation, and created the eye, ear, and nose, and shaped the face in the best form, and deposited in it beauty and perfection that is not hidden. Then He deposited sight in the eye, hearing in the ear, and smell in the nose, and created the mouth and adorned it with two lips, and created the tongue and created taste in it, and made it a soldier among His soldiers — exalted is He — translating what is in the heart of knowledge and perceptions. He made the neck a carrier of the throne of the head in beautiful innovation, and made in it the passage connecting food and drink to the stomach. And He deposited in the stomach the intestines, bowels, heart, liver, and others whose reality none knows except Him, exalted is He. And He created the hands and made in them the palms and fingers, made them joints and innovated them, and likewise the legs. He created bones and clothed them with flesh. Then He blew into you the spirit — and it is a great wondrous secret among His secrets — so you moved in your mother's womb. He remained kind and merciful to you, protecting you in the tightest place, delivering your nourishment while you knew nothing. Until when your creation was completed, He brought you down from the womb from the narrowest place, and was gentle with you and your mother. When you came out to your mother's breast, He caused milk to flow in it and placed in her heart affection and mercy, so that she considers your urine and stool as the best of things. The favor is His in that. And when the time for eating came, He created for you the teeth and molars, arranging them in a wondrous manner with the perfection of beauty, elegance, and completeness. Then when you approached maturity, and these teeth were weak, He dropped them and replaced them with stronger ones. Then when you eat, Allah causes to flow in your mouth a running spring — which is saliva — whose flow does not cease as long as you eat, to moisten the morsel and make swallowing easy. You do not control it, nor does it flow continuously, nor does it stop. So look at this wondrous wisdom to which you are in utmost need, and it is not in your power to cause it or prevent it by necessity. When food and drink descend into the stomach, He distributes them as He wills: some nourishes the flesh, some nourishes the bone, some nourishes the fat, some nourishes the blood, with complete pleasure during and after eating. Then what remains beyond that, which would harm the body if kept in the stomach, He expels from your two exits. Look at these two exits and the wondrous wisdom of them, and at how He enabled you to hold them back when the waste is ready to exit. In short, He — glorified is He — has remained kind, merciful, loving, and generous to you every moment while you are heedless of yourself. And look at the exhalation and inhalation of breath, by which the spirit is sustained, whether awake or asleep, in health or sickness.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof of God's existence, attributes, and wisdom through reflection on the stages of human creation. Dardeer begins by citing the Quranic verse "And in yourselves, do you not see?" (Quran 51:21), establishing the method of inner reflection. He then traces human development from conception to adulthood, emphasizing divine control, wisdom, and mercy at every step. The argument is teleological: each intricate detail of the body — the senses, organs, bones, skin, digestion, and even the nursing instinct — points to a wise and powerful Creator. The proof concludes with the observation that God's continuous care for humans continues every moment, even though humans are often heedless. The passage refutes atheism by showing that such complexity cannot arise by chance.

الريق (rīq - saliva)
النفس (nafs - breath/soul)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might take these bodily functions for granted and not see them as signs of God.
Correction: The passage urges active reflection on each detail—teeth, saliva, digestion, breath—as deliberate divine acts.

What does Dardeer call the flow of saliva in the mouth during eating?

?
You just read that every time you eat, Allah causes saliva to flow in your mouth—without you willing it. When you sit down for your next meal, what will you do to actively remember that this is a gift from Him, rather than a mere biological reflex?
?
The passage says you are 'heedless of yourself' while Allah is kind and merciful every moment. What is one daily bodily function—like breathing or digesting—that you have never before considered as a direct act of divine care? Starting tomorrow, how will you turn that into a moment of gratitude?
?
If it were up to you to control your saliva, digestion, or breath, you would fail. Does this realization unsettle you or comfort you? What does it reveal about your actual dependence on Allah—and what change in your daily attitude does it demand?

Allah's Existence

Creation of the Human Body and the Spirit
Dardeer enumerates the creation of human limbs and the spirit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the creation of the human body and the blowing of the spirit manifest Allah's power, mercy, and wisdom.

Core Idea
Your body is a divine miracle—each part testifies to its Creator.

Imam Dardeer begins his reflection by guiding us to contemplate the intricate creation of our own hands, feet, bones, and the soul that gives us life. This passage is not mere anatomy; it is a theological meditation meant to awaken gratitude and certainty in Allah's constant care, even before we were born.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and its translation. Notice the detailed description of hands, fingers, bones, flesh, and the blowing of the spirit.
The spirit is described as a 'great wonderful secret'.
2
Reflect on the sequence
Note the order: creation of limbs, then clothing bones with flesh, then the spirit, then movement in the womb. Ask why this order matters.
The spirit is breathed after the body is formed, showing Allah's direct action.
3
Connect to divine attributes
Identify which attributes of Allah are highlighted: power (creation), mercy (care in the womb), wisdom (perfect design).
This builds a foundation for tawheed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات هو تعالى، وخلق الأيدي وخلق فيها الأكف والأصابع وجعلها مفاصل وأبدعها، والأرجل كذلك، وخلق العظام وكساها لحما، ثُمَّ نَفَخَ فيك الرُّوحَ - وهي سر عظيم عجيب من أسراره تعالى - فتحركت في بطن أمك، وما زال بك رؤوفًا رحيما، حافظا لك في أضيق مكان، يوصل لك غذاءك وأنت لا تعلم شيئا. حتى إذا تم خلقك أنزلك من الرحم من أضيق محل فلطف بك وبأمك، حتى إذا بررت أفمك بمجرد النزول إلى تدى أمك وأجرى فيه اللبن، وأنزل في قلبها الرأفة والرحمة، حتى إنها ترى بولك وعائطك من أحسن ما يكون، والمنة له تعالى في ذلك. ولما آن أوان الأكل خلق لك الأسنان والأضراس ورتبها ترتيبا عجيبا مع ما فيها من كمال الزينة والجمال والكمال، ثم لما قرب بلوغك وكانت هذه الأسنان ضعيفة أسقطها وأبدلها بأقوى منها، ثم إذا أكلت فجر الله في فمك عينا جارية – وهي الريق - لا ينقطع جريانها ما دمت تأكل لتبتل اللقمة بها ويسهل بلعها، لا تملكها النفس ولا تجري على الدوام ولا تنقطع، فانظر إلى هذه الحكمة العجيبة التي أنت في غاية الافتقار إليها، وليس في قدرتك إجراؤها ولا منعها بالضرورة، فإذا نزل الطعام والشراب في المعدة صرفه إلى ما يشاء، فبعضه يتربى به اللحم، وبعضه يتربى به العظم، وبعضه يتربى به الشحم، وبعضه يتربى به الدم مع كمال اللذة حال الأكل وبعده، ثم ما فضل عن ذلك وكان فيه الإيذاء للبدن على تقدير إبقائه في البطن أخرجه من مخرجيك، وانظر إلى هذين المخرجين وبديع حكمتهما وإلى إقدارك على إمساكهما عند تهيؤ الفضلة للخروج. وبالجملة: فلم يزل سبحانه بك رؤوفا رحيما ودودا كريما في كل لحظة وأنت عاقل عن فعال من نفسك. وانظر إلى خروج النفس ودخوله الذي به قوام الروح حالة اليقظة والنوم والصحة والمرض. شرح الخريدة البهية ومن أكبر عبرة: العقل الذي به التمييز والتدبير، وإدراك العلوم والمعارف وما يضر وما ينفع «وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَةَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا» (١)، فَتَبَارَكَ اللهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ) (٢). فيا ليت شعري! أهذا ينبغي أن يعصى فيها أمر ونهى؟! ثم إذا نظرت إلى السماء وكواكبها والسحاب وتسخيرها، والرياح وتصريفها وإلى الأرض وأنهارها، وإلى الأشجار وثمارها لأفضى بك إلى العجب العجاب وعلمت أنه المحسن الوهاب. اللهم وفقنا لما فيه رضاك، واقطعنا عن كل سواك، واملأ قلوبنا من حبك وحب رسلك، وأذقنا لذة الوصل من فيض فضلك، وخذ بأيدينا إن زللنا، وسامحنا إن أخطأنا، إنك أنت الجواد الكريم، الرؤوف الرحيم. (۱) سورة النحل: من الآية ١٨ (۲) سورة المؤمنون: من الآية ١٤ ، والخلق هنا بمعنى التقدير، أي فتبارك الله أحسن المقدرين، لأن الخلق ورد في القرآن الكريم لمعان ثلاثة: أولها الإيجاد من العدم وهذا خاص به سبحانه ثانيها التقدير، ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيراً﴾ [الفرقان: ٢]، ثالثها: الكذب، قال تعالى: ﴿وَتَخْلُقُونَ إِفْكاً﴾ [العنكبوت: ١٧]، وهو هنا بالمعنى الثاني.
The first section: Divine matters. He is exalted, and He created the hands and created in them the palms and fingers and made them joints and originated them, and the legs likewise, and created the bones and clothed them with flesh, then blew into you the spirit - and it is a great wonderful secret from His secrets, exalted is He - so you moved in your mother's womb, and He continued to be kind and merciful to you, protecting you in the tightest place, delivering your nourishment to you while you knew nothing. Until when your creation was completed, He brought you down from the womb from the tightest place, and He was gentle with you and your mother, until when you [suckled] your mother's breast upon merely descending to your mother's breast, and He made the milk flow in it, and sent down into her heart affection and mercy, so that she sees your urine and your milk [?] as the best of things, and the favor is His, exalted, in that. And when the time for eating came, He created for you the teeth and molars and arranged them in a wonderful arrangement, along with what is in them of complete adornment, beauty, and perfection. Then when your adolescence approached and these teeth were weak, He caused them to fall and replaced them with stronger ones. Then when you eat, God causes a flowing spring to burst forth in your mouth - which is saliva - its flow does not cease as long as you eat, so that the morsel becomes moistened by it and its swallowing becomes easy. You do not possess it by your will, nor does it flow continuously, nor does it stop. So look at this amazing wisdom to which you are in utmost need, and it is not in your power to produce it or prevent it by necessity. When food and drink descend into the stomach, He directs them to whatever He wills: some of it nourishes the flesh, some of it nourishes the bone, some of it nourishes the fat, and some of it nourishes the blood, along with complete pleasure during and after eating. Then what is surplus to that and would cause harm to the body if it were kept in the abdomen, He expels it from your two exits. And look at these two exits and the wonderful wisdom of them, and at your ability to hold them back when the waste is ready to exit. In summary: He, glorified, has never ceased to be kind, merciful, affectionate, and generous to you at every moment, while you are rational about what you do from yourself. And look at the exhalation and inhalation of breath by which the spirit is sustained, in the states of wakefulness, sleep, health, and sickness. Explanation of Al-Kharidat Al-Bahiyyah: And among the greatest signs is the intellect, by which comes discrimination and management, and the perception of sciences and knowledges and what harms and benefits. 'And if you should count the favors of Allah, you could not enumerate them' (16:18). So blessed is Allah, the best of creators (23:14). Oh, would that I knew! Is it fitting that He be disobeyed in what He commands and forbids? Then if you look at the sky and its planets, and the clouds and their subjugation, and the winds and their disposition, and at the earth and its rivers, and at the trees and their fruits, it will lead you to utmost wonder, and you will know that He is the Benefactor, the Bestower. O Allah, grant us success in what pleases You, and cut us off from everything other than You, and fill our hearts with love of You and love of Your messengers, and make us taste the sweetness of union from the flow of Your bounty, and take our hands if we slip, and forgive us if we err. Indeed, You are the Generous, the Kind, the Compassionate, the Merciful. (1) Surah An-Nahl: from verse 18. (2) Surah Al-Mu'minun: from verse 14, and 'creation' here means 'estimation' (taqdeer), meaning blessed is Allah, the best of estimators. Because the word 'khalq' appears in the Noble Quran with three meanings: first, bringing into existence from nothing, which is specific to Him; second, estimation, and from it is His statement 'and He created everything and determined it with precision' (25:2); third, lying, as He said 'and you invent [takhluqoon] falsehood' (29:17), and it is here in the second meaning.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a meditative reflection on the blessings of God, intended to inspire gratitude and recognition of His power and mercy. The author, Imam Dardeer, begins by describing the creation of the human body: hands with palms and fingers, legs, bones covered with flesh, and the blowing of the spirit which causes movement in the womb. He emphasizes God's constant care, providing nourishment even before birth. Then he describes the process of birth and breastfeeding, noting how God places affection in the mother's heart and makes her view the infant's waste as something good. Next, he discusses teeth: their creation, arrangement, beauty, and replacement with stronger teeth at adolescence. He draws attention to the continuous flow of saliva during eating, which is beyond voluntary control, as a sign of divine wisdom. Digestion is described: food is directed to nourish different parts of the body, and waste is expelled through two exits, which one can control until the moment of expulsion. The author summarizes that God is constantly kind and merciful. He then turns to the intellect as a great sign, enabling discrimination and knowledge. He quotes two Quranic verses (16:18 and 23:14) and exclaims that it is unfitting to disobey God. He urges contemplation of the heavens, clouds, winds, earth, rivers, trees, and fruits, which lead to wonder and recognition of God as the Benefactor. He concludes with a supplication for guidance, love of God and His messengers, and forgiveness. The footnote explains that in verse 23:14, 'khalq' means 'estimation' (taqdeer), not creation from nothing, and lists the three Quranic meanings of 'khalq': bringing into existence from nothing, estimation, and lying.

Key Terms
خلق (khalq)
روح (rūḥ)
نعمة (ni'mah)
حكمة (ḥikmah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The human body evolved randomly with no purpose.
Correction: The passage shows deliberate creation and order, pointing to a wise Creator who sustains even in the womb.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Dardeer call the spirit?
A) A biological mechanism
B) A great wonderful secret from Allah's secrets
C) A natural force
D) A product of the body

Key Takeaway
Every part of your body, from hands to spirit, is a direct gift from Allah, calling you to gratitude and faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own hands, do you see them as a gift from Allah or just tools you own? What would change if you thanked Him for each finger every day?
?
Your spirit is a secret from Allah that you cannot fully understand. Are you living as if your soul is precious and accountable, or do you neglect it for worldly pursuits?
?
You moved in your mother's womb, protected and nourished without any effort from you. Are you now living in gratitude for that care, or have you forgotten the One who sustained you then and sustains you now?

Divine Care from Birth to Childhood
Dardeer details the blessings of birth, breastfeeeding, and teeth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate how Allah’s mercy is manifest in the processes of birth, breastfeeding, and the growth of teeth.

Core Idea
From the womb to the table, Allah's mercy precedes your effort.

Imam Dardeer continues his reflection by moving from the prenatal stage to the moment of birth and early childhood. He highlights Allah’s gentleness in bringing the baby out, the provision of milk through the mother’s breast, and even the seemingly mundane matter of teeth – all as signs of divine wisdom and love.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with awe
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the specific details: the tight womb, the easy birth, the milk, the mother’s affection, and the teeth.
Even urine and milk are mentioned as signs of mercy.
2
Analyze the progression
Trace the stages: birth, suckling, weaning, teeth eruption, and replacement. Each stage has a specific blessing.
The replacement of weak teeth with stronger ones is highlighted as wisdom.
3
Extract the theological message
Ask: what does each blessing tell us about Allah? Birth shows gentleness, milk shows provision, teeth show design and foresight.
The goal is to see Allah’s constant 'ra’uf rahim' (kind, merciful).

القسم الأول: الإلهيات هو تعالى، وخلق الأيدي وخلق فيها الأكف والأصابع وجعلها مفاصل وأبدعها، والأرجل كذلك، وخلق العظام وكساها لحما، ثُمَّ نَفَخَ فيك الرُّوحَ - وهي سر عظيم عجيب من أسراره تعالى - فتحركت في بطن أمك، وما زال بك رؤوفًا رحيما، حافظا لك في أضيق مكان، يوصل لك غذاءك وأنت لا تعلم شيئا. حتى إذا تم خلقك أنزلك من الرحم من أضيق محل فلطف بك وبأمك، حتى إذا بررت أفمك بمجرد النزول إلى تدى أمك وأجرى فيه اللبن، وأنزل في قلبها الرأفة والرحمة، حتى إنها ترى بولك وعائطك من أحسن ما يكون، والمنة له تعالى في ذلك. ولما آن أوان الأكل خلق لك الأسنان والأضراس ورتبها ترتيبا عجيبا مع ما فيها من كمال الزينة والجمال والكمال، ثم لما قرب بلوغك وكانت هذه الأسنان ضعيفة أسقطها وأبدلها بأقوى منها، ثم إذا أكلت فجر الله في فمك عينا جارية – وهي الريق - لا ينقطع جريانها ما دمت تأكل لتبتل اللقمة بها ويسهل بلعها، لا تملكها النفس ولا تجري على الدوام ولا تنقطع، فانظر إلى هذه الحكمة العجيبة التي أنت في غاية الافتقار إليها، وليس في قدرتك إجراؤها ولا منعها بالضرورة، فإذا نزل الطعام والشراب في المعدة صرفه إلى ما يشاء، فبعضه يتربى به اللحم، وبعضه يتربى به العظم، وبعضه يتربى به الشحم، وبعضه يتربى به الدم مع كمال اللذة حال الأكل وبعده، ثم ما فضل عن ذلك وكان فيه الإيذاء للبدن على تقدير إبقائه في البطن أخرجه من مخرجيك، وانظر إلى هذين المخرجين وبديع حكمتهما وإلى إقدارك على إمساكهما عند تهيؤ الفضلة للخروج. وبالجملة: فلم يزل سبحانه بك رؤوفا رحيما ودودا كريما في كل لحظة وأنت عاقل عن فعال من نفسك. وانظر إلى خروج النفس ودخوله الذي به قوام الروح حالة اليقظة والنوم والصحة والمرض. شرح الخريدة البهية ومن أكبر عبرة: العقل الذي به التمييز والتدبير، وإدراك العلوم والمعارف وما يضر وما ينفع «وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَةَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا» (١)، فَتَبَارَكَ اللهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ) (٢). فيا ليت شعري! أهذا ينبغي أن يعصى فيها أمر ونهى؟! ثم إذا نظرت إلى السماء وكواكبها والسحاب وتسخيرها، والرياح وتصريفها وإلى الأرض وأنهارها، وإلى الأشجار وثمارها لأفضى بك إلى العجب العجاب وعلمت أنه المحسن الوهاب. اللهم وفقنا لما فيه رضاك، واقطعنا عن كل سواك، واملأ قلوبنا من حبك وحب رسلك، وأذقنا لذة الوصل من فيض فضلك، وخذ بأيدينا إن زللنا، وسامحنا إن أخطأنا، إنك أنت الجواد الكريم، الرؤوف الرحيم. (۱) سورة النحل: من الآية ١٨ (۲) سورة المؤمنون: من الآية ١٤ ، والخلق هنا بمعنى التقدير، أي فتبارك الله أحسن المقدرين، لأن الخلق ورد في القرآن الكريم لمعان ثلاثة: أولها الإيجاد من العدم وهذا خاص به سبحانه ثانيها التقدير، ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيراً﴾ [الفرقان: ٢]، ثالثها: الكذب، قال تعالى: ﴿وَتَخْلُقُونَ إِفْكاً﴾ [العنكبوت: ١٧]، وهو هنا بالمعنى الثاني.
The first section: Divine matters. He is exalted, and He created the hands and created in them the palms and fingers and made them joints and originated them, and the legs likewise, and created the bones and clothed them with flesh, then blew into you the spirit - and it is a great wonderful secret from His secrets, exalted is He - so you moved in your mother's womb, and He continued to be kind and merciful to you, protecting you in the tightest place, delivering your nourishment to you while you knew nothing. Until when your creation was completed, He brought you down from the womb from the tightest place, and He was gentle with you and your mother, until when you [suckled] your mother's breast upon merely descending to your mother's breast, and He made the milk flow in it, and sent down into her heart affection and mercy, so that she sees your urine and your milk [?] as the best of things, and the favor is His, exalted, in that. And when the time for eating came, He created for you the teeth and molars and arranged them in a wonderful arrangement, along with what is in them of complete adornment, beauty, and perfection. Then when your adolescence approached and these teeth were weak, He caused them to fall and replaced them with stronger ones. Then when you eat, God causes a flowing spring to burst forth in your mouth - which is saliva - its flow does not cease as long as you eat, so that the morsel becomes moistened by it and its swallowing becomes easy. You do not possess it by your will, nor does it flow continuously, nor does it stop. So look at this amazing wisdom to which you are in utmost need, and it is not in your power to produce it or prevent it by necessity. When food and drink descend into the stomach, He directs them to whatever He wills: some of it nourishes the flesh, some of it nourishes the bone, some of it nourishes the fat, and some of it nourishes the blood, along with complete pleasure during and after eating. Then what is surplus to that and would cause harm to the body if it were kept in the abdomen, He expels it from your two exits. And look at these two exits and the wonderful wisdom of them, and at your ability to hold them back when the waste is ready to exit. In summary: He, glorified, has never ceased to be kind, merciful, affectionate, and generous to you at every moment, while you are rational about what you do from yourself. And look at the exhalation and inhalation of breath by which the spirit is sustained, in the states of wakefulness, sleep, health, and sickness. The Wisdom of Saliva and Digestion
Dardeer describes the wisdom of saliva and digestion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the processes of eating, digestion, and excretion reveal Allah’s wisdom and control over our bodies.

Core Idea
Your saliva and stomach obey Allah, not you—a sign of His sole dominion.

Imam Dardeer now turns to the inner workings of the body: the continuous flow of saliva during eating, the digestion in the stomach, and the controlled expulsion of waste. These are everyday miracles that we take for granted, but they are profound signs of Allah’s power and wisdom. The lesson shows that even the most automatic bodily functions are under His command.

Guided Path
1
Examine the saliva description
Read the passage and note how saliva is described: a flowing spring that appears only during eating, not under voluntary control. Why is this considered 'amazing wisdom'?
It is a perfect provision that you cannot produce or stop at will.
2
Trace the digestion process
Follow the journey of food: stomach, distribution to flesh, bone, fat, blood, and then expulsion of waste.
The passage emphasizes the complete pleasure during and after eating.
3
Reflect on the two exits
Consider the control over the exits: you can hold back waste until the right moment. This is a sign of Allah’s design.
This shows both power and wisdom in the body's functions.

Then if you look at the sky and its planets, and the clouds and their subjugation, and the winds and their disposition, and at the earth and its rivers, and at the trees and their fruits, it will lead you to utmost wonder, and you will know that He is the Benefactor, the Bestower. O Allah, grant us success in what pleases You, and cut us off from everything other than You, and fill our hearts with love of You and love of Your messengers, and make us taste the sweetness of union from the flow of Your bounty, and take our hands if we slip, and forgive us if we err. Indeed, You are the Generous, the Kind, the Compassionate, the Merciful. (1) Surah An-Nahl: from verse 18. (2) Surah Al-Mu'minun: from verse 14, and 'creation' here means 'estimation' (taqdeer), meaning blessed is Allah, the best of estimators. Because the word 'khalq' appears in the Noble Quran with three meanings: first, bringing into existence from nothing, which is specific to Him; second, estimation, and from it is His statement 'and He created everything and determined it with precision' (25:2); third, lying, as He said 'and you invent [takhluqoon] falsehood' (29:17), and it is here in the second meaning.

Commentary
This passage is a meditative reflection on the blessings of God, intended to inspire gratitude and recognition of His power and mercy. The author, Imam Dardeer, begins by describing the creation of the human body: hands with palms and fingers, legs, bones covered with flesh, and the blowing of the spirit which causes movement in the womb. The Intellect, Gratitude, and Cosmic Signs
Dardeer on the intellect, gratitude, cosmic signs, and supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the central role of the intellect as the greatest sign, and how contemplation of the cosmos leads to recognition of Allah’s oneness and the imperative of obedience.

Core Idea
The intellect is the scale; the cosmos is the proof; gratitude is the duty.

Imam Dardeer now draws a conclusion from the bodily reflections: he highlights the intellect as the greatest sign, quotes two Quranic verses, and then calls the reader to contemplate the heavens and the earth as overwhelming proofs of Allah’s beneficence. He ends with a powerful supplication asking for steadfastness in obedience and love. This lesson ties the entire reflection together into a call for tawheed and worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with attention to the transition
Notice the shift from bodily blessings to the intellect and then to the cosmos. Why does Dardeer call the intellect the 'greatest sign'?
The intellect allows us to perceive and appreciate all other signs.
2
Analyze the rhetorical question
"Is it fitting that He be disobeyed?" This is a moral conclusion from the blessings. Reflect on the logic: blessings imply gratitude, gratitude implies obedience.
The verse 'And if you count the favors of Allah, you cannot enumerate them' supports this.
3
Contemplate the cosmic signs
Sky, planets, clouds, winds, earth, rivers, trees, fruits – each is a subjugated sign. This should lead to 'utmost wonder' and knowledge of Allah as 'al-Muhsin al-Wahhab'.
The footnote explains the meaning of 'khalq' in the verse as 'estimation' (taqdeer).

The first section: Divine matters. Existence as a Mental Addition
Sanusi argues that existence is mentally additional to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that existence is mentally additional to essence, meaning the intellect can distinguish them even though they are not separate in external reality.

Core Idea
Existence is mentally distinct from essence, not a separate entity outside.

The author begins by stating the importance of understanding existence, as other attributes depend on it. He clarifies a key debate in Sunni theology: whether existence is identical to essence or an additional attribute. In this passage, he argues for the middle position—existence is mentally additional, not externally real.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument.
Notice the quote from Taftazani; he asserts there is no disagreement.
2
Identify the claim about existence
The passage states that existence is mentally additional (za'id dhihnan). Underline this key phrase.
The intellect can consider essence without existence, and vice versa.
3
Understand Taftazani's support
Al-Taftazani affirms that existence is mentally additional, meaning the intellect can separate them conceptually.
This shows consensus among later scholars.
4
Reflect on the implication
We can conceive of an essence while doubting its existence, proving conceptual separation.
This distinguishes the Sunni view from extreme positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قُلتُ: لما كان معرفةُ الوُجودِ يُحتاجُ لها؛ لِيَنبني عليها غيرُها مِنَ الصِّفاتِ اعتبرت الوصْفَ الظاهري في قولنا ذاتُ اللهِ مَوجودةٌ) وارتكبتُ التسَمُّحَ.
أنَّ التحقيقَ أَنَّ الشَّيخَ ولو نفى الأحوال، لا ينفي الاعتبارات لظهور زيادتها على ذهنا، وإن لم يكن لها ثبوت خارجا ) ، بل قال العلامة التفتازاني: لا خِلافَ أَنَّ الوُجودَ زائد ذهنًا)، بمعنى أنَّ للعَقْلِ أنْ يُلاحِظَ الماهية بدونِ الوُجودِ، وبالعكس، ونتعقل الماهية ونشك في وجودها. اهـ.
(۱) لظهور زيادتها ذهنا أي لا خارجًا، لأن للشيء أربعة وجودات: وجود في الأذهان، ووجود في اللسان أي العبارات، ووجود في البنان أي الكتابة، ووجود في الأعيان أي الخارج، وهو الوجود الحقيقي. [سباعي، ص ٢٦٢]
(۲) ولذلك قال الباجوري والمحققون كالسعد وأضرابه أولوا عبارة الأشعري، فقالوا: ليس المراد العينية حقيقة، بل المراد أنه ليس زائدا على الذات في الخارج بحيث تصح رؤيته، فلا ينافي أنه أمر اعتباري [حاشية الباجوري على الجوهرة ١٠٦ ، وعلى السنوسية ١٧]
I said: Since knowledge of existence is needed, because other attributes are built upon it, I considered the apparent description in our saying 'The essence of Allah exists' and I committed leniency. The verification is that the shaykh, even if he denies states (ahwal), does not deny considerations (i'tibarat) because their addition is apparent in the mind, even if they have no external subsistence. Rather, 'Allamah al-Taftazani said: There is no disagreement that existence is additional mentally, meaning that the intellect can observe the quiddity without existence, and vice versa, and we conceive the quiddity and doubt its existence. End. (1) 'Because their addition is apparent mentally, i.e., not externally, for a thing has four existences: existence in minds, existence in tongues i.e., expressions, existence in script i.e., writing, and existence in external entities i.e., external reality, and that is the true existence.' [Subay'i, p. 262] (2) 'Thus al-Bajuri and the verifiers like al-Sa'd and his peers interpreted al-Ash'ari's statement, saying: The intended meaning is not actual identity (al-'ayniyya) in reality, but rather that it is not additional to the essence in the external such that it could be seen, so it does not contradict that it is a mental consideration.' [Hashiyat al-Bajuri 'ala al-Jawhara 106, and 'ala al-Sanusiyya 17]
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the nature of existence as an attribute of God. The author begins by noting that knowledge of existence is needed because it is foundational for other attributes. He admits to a certain leniency in describing existence as a 'visible description' in the statement 'The essence of Allah exists'. He then clarifies the correct position: even if the Shaykh (i.e., al-Ash'ari) denies the theory of states (ahwal), he does not deny mental considerations (i'tibarat), because these are clearly added in the mind, even if they have no separate external reality. The author quotes al-Taftazani, who affirms that there is no disagreement that existence is mentally additional (za'id dhihnan). The intellect can conceive of an essence without considering its existence, and vice versa; we can form a concept of an essence while doubting its actual existence. The two footnotes support this view. The first footnote explains the four types of existence: mental, verbal, written, and external. The external existence is the true, real existence. The second footnote notes that later scholars like al-Bajuri and al-Sa'd interpreted al-Ash'ari's statement about attributes being identical with the essence as meaning that attributes are not additional in external reality in a way that would make them separate entities, but they are mental considerations (i'tibarat). Thus existence is a mental concept, not an extra entity outside.

Key Terms
وجود
زيادة ذهنية
ماهية
اعتبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That existence is a real attribute added to the essence in external reality, like a separate entity.
Correction: The passage clarifies that existence is only mentally additional; it is not a separate entity outside.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'existence is additional mentally'?
A) Existence is a separate entity outside the essence.
B) The intellect can distinguish existence from essence, but they are not separate in external reality.
C) Existence is identical to the essence in every respect.
D) Existence is added to the essence in time.

Key Takeaway
Existence is a mental distinction from essence, not an extra external attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself mentally separating Allah's essence from His existence, as if He could be conceived without His existence? What does that reveal about the strength of your conviction?
?
When you say 'Allah exists', is it merely a mental concept you accept, or does it permeate your heart and actions? What would change if you lived as if His existence were as certain as your own?
?
If the intellect can doubt the existence of a conceived essence, how do you respond when doubts about Allah's existence cross your mind? Do you rely on mental proof alone, or something deeper?

The Four Existences and the Ash'ari Interpretation
Footnotes explaining the four forms of existence and Ash'ari's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four realms of existence (mental, verbal, written, external) and how scholars reconciled Ash'ari's view with the mental addition theory.

Core Idea
A thing has four existences; Ash'ari's identity statement means no external separation.

The author's claim that existence is mentally additional is supported by a traditional classification of existence and by interpreting Ash'ari's words. This lesson unpacks these supporting points from the footnotes.

Guided Path
1
Read the footnotes
Read the two footnotes in Arabic and translation. They provide additional support for the main argument.
The first footnote lists four types of existence.
2
List the four existences
Identify the four existences: mental, verbal, written, and external (actual).
External existence is the true existence.
3
Understand the Ash'ari interpretation
The second footnote explains that al-Ash'ari's statement about attributes being identical to the essence means they are not additional in external reality, but they are mental considerations.
This reconciles Ash'ari with the mental addition view.
4
Reflect on the consensus
Scholars like al-Bajuri and al-Sa'd interpreted Ash'ari to avoid contradiction.
This shows the mainstream Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قُلتُ: لما كان معرفةُ الوُجودِ يُحتاجُ لها؛ لِيَنبني عليها غيرُها مِنَ الصِّفاتِ اعتبرت الوصْفَ الظاهري في قولنا ذاتُ اللهِ مَوجودةٌ) وارتكبتُ التسَمُّحَ.
أنَّ التحقيقَ أَنَّ الشَّيخَ ولو نفى الأحوال، لا ينفي الاعتبارات لظهور زيادتها على ذهنا، وإن لم يكن لها ثبوت خارجا ) ، بل قال العلامة التفتازاني: لا خِلافَ أَنَّ الوُجودَ زائد ذهنًا)، بمعنى أنَّ للعَقْلِ أنْ يُلاحِظَ الماهية بدونِ الوُجودِ، وبالعكس، ونتعقل الماهية ونشك في وجودها. اهـ.
(۱) لظهور زيادتها ذهنا أي لا خارجًا، لأن للشيء أربعة وجودات: وجود في الأذهان، ووجود في اللسان أي العبارات، ووجود في البنان أي الكتابة، ووجود في الأعيان أي الخارج، وهو الوجود الحقيقي. [سباعي، ص ٢٦٢]
(۲) ولذلك قال الباجوري والمحققون كالسعد وأضرابه أولوا عبارة الأشعري، فقالوا: ليس المراد العينية حقيقة، بل المراد أنه ليس زائدا على الذات في الخارج بحيث تصح رؤيته، فلا ينافي أنه أمر اعتباري [حاشية الباجوري على الجوهرة ١٠٦ ، وعلى السنوسية ١٧]
I said: Since knowledge of existence is needed, because other attributes are built upon it, I considered the apparent description in our saying 'The essence of Allah exists' and I committed leniency. The verification is that the shaykh, even if he denies states (ahwal), does not deny considerations (i'tibarat) because their addition is apparent in the mind, even if they have no external subsistence. Rather, 'Allamah al-Taftazani said: There is no disagreement that existence is additional mentally, meaning that the intellect can observe the quiddity without existence, and vice versa, and we conceive the quiddity and doubt its existence. End. (1) 'Because their addition is apparent mentally, i.e., not externally, for a thing has four existences: existence in minds, existence in tongues i.e., expressions, existence in script i.e., writing, and existence in external entities i.e., external reality, and that is the true existence.' [Subay'i, p. 262] (2) 'Thus al-Bajuri and the verifiers like al-Sa'd and his peers interpreted al-Ash'ari's statement, saying: The intended meaning is not actual identity (al-'ayniyya) in reality, but rather that it is not additional to the essence in the external such that it could be seen, so it does not contradict that it is a mental consideration.' [Hashiyat al-Bajuri 'ala al-Jawhara 106, and 'ala al-Sanusiyya 17]
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the nature of existence as an attribute of God. The author begins by noting that knowledge of existence is needed because it is foundational for other attributes. He admits to a certain leniency in describing existence as a 'visible description' in the statement 'The essence of Allah exists'. He then clarifies the correct position: even if the Shaykh (i.e., al-Ash'ari) denies the theory of states (ahwal), he does not deny mental considerations (i'tibarat), because these are clearly added in the mind, even if they have no separate external reality. The author quotes al-Taftazani, who affirms that there is no disagreement that existence is mentally additional (za'id dhihnan). The intellect can conceive of an essence without considering its existence, and vice versa; we can form a concept of an essence while doubting its actual existence. The two footnotes support this view. The first footnote explains the four types of existence: mental, verbal, written, and external. The external existence is the true, real existence. The second footnote notes that later scholars like al-Bajuri and al-Sa'd interpreted al-Ash'ari's statement about attributes being identical with the essence as meaning that attributes are not additional in external reality in a way that would make them separate entities, but they are mental considerations (i'tibarat). Thus existence is a mental concept, not an extra entity outside.

Key Terms
وجود
أذهان
لسان
بنان
أعيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari's view that attributes are identical to the essence contradicts the idea of mental addition.
Correction: Scholars interpret Ash'ari as denying external addition, not mental consideration, so there is no contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to the first footnote, how many types of existence does a thing have?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The four existences framework and Ash'ari interpretation support that existence is a mental addition, not an external extra.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's attributes like His power or mercy, do you catch yourself imagining them as separate 'things' attached to Him? After learning that they are not additional in external reality but only mental considerations, how will you train your mind to avoid this subtle form of shirk?
?
If only external existence is truly real, then your thoughts and intentions (which exist in your mind) are not real in the same way. Does that make them less accountable before Allah? Or does it highlight the importance of your inner state since mental existence is still a form of existence that Allah knows? How will this change how you purify your intentions?

Proof of God's Pre-Eternity: Refuting Circularity and Infinite Regress
Imam Dardeer refutes دور and تسلسل to prove God's pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the impossibility of circularity (al-dawr) and infinite regress (al-tasalsul) establishes God's attribute of qidam.

Core Idea
Circularity and infinite regress are impossible, so God must be eternal.

In this lesson, Imam Dardeer presents a concise argument for God's pre-eternity. He shows that any attempt to deny God's eternity leads to either circular reasoning or an infinite chain of dependent causes, both of which are rationally impossible. By eliminating these, the pre-eternity of God is necessarily affirmed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then its English translation. Notice the logical structure: two refutations followed by a conclusion.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the refutation of circularity
The author argues that circularity (al-dawr) is impossible because it would require each thing to both precede and be preceded by the other, which is contradictory. He also mentions self-precedence as an additional absurdity.
3
Understand the refutation of infinite regress
The author argues that infinite regress (al-tasalsul) leads to an infinite chain of gods, each temporally originated and needy, which contradicts the necessary attributes of God (power, self-sufficiency). Hence it is impossible.
Note the connection to the perfection of creation.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Since both alternatives are impossible, the original proposition—God's pre-eternity—is necessarily true.
This is a classic kalam argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمّا استحالةُ الدَّورِ فظاهرةٌ، لأنه يلزَمُ عليه تقدم كل منهما على صاحبه وتأخُرُه عنه، وهو جمع بَينَ مُتَنافِيين، بل ويلزَمُ عليه أيضًا تقدَّمُ كُلِّ واحدٍ منها على نقص وتأخُرُه عنها، وهو جلي البطلان. نفسه وأمّا التَّسَلْسُلُ فلأنه يؤدي إلى وُجودِ آلهة لا نهاية لها، كُلٌّ منها متَّصِفٌ بالحدون والعجز والافتقار، وهو باطل قطعًا، لأنه مُناف لمقام الألوهية من القدرة والغنى المطلق، إذ العاجز الفقيرُ لا يصح أن يكون خالقا للعالم البديع الإتقان. وما أفضى إلى المحال - وهو عدَمُ القِدَم - مُحالٌ، إذ استحالةُ اللوازم تقتضي استحالة الملزومات، فثبَتَ القِدَمُ، وهو المطلوب.
As for the impossibility of circularity, it is apparent, because it would necessitate each of them preceding its companion and being preceded by it, which is a combination of two contradictories. Rather, it would also necessitate each of them preceding and being preceded by itself, which is clearly false. As for infinite regress, it leads to the existence of infinite gods, each characterized by temporal origination, incapability, and neediness, which is absolutely false, because it contradicts the station of divinity in terms of power and absolute self-sufficiency, for the incapable and needy cannot be the creator of the world of perfect design. And whatever leads to the impossible—which is the non-existence of pre-eternity—is impossible, for the impossibility of the consequences necessitates the impossibility of the antecedents. Thus pre-eternity is established, and that is what is sought.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a proof of God's attribute of qidam (pre-eternity) by demonstrating the impossibility of two alternatives: circularity (al-dawr) and infinite regress (al-tasalsul). The author begins by explaining that circularity is impossible because it would require each of two things to both precede and be preceded by the other, which is a contradiction. He then adds that circularity would also entail each thing preceding and being preceded by itself, which is even more absurd. Next, he argues that infinite regress leads to an infinite chain of gods, each of which would be temporally originated, incapable, and needy. This is impossible because the true God must be powerful and self-sufficient; a needy being cannot be the creator of such a perfectly designed world. Therefore, any argument that leads to the denial of God's pre-eternity is invalid. Hence, qidam is established.

Key Terms
الدور
التسلسل
القدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think an infinite causal regress is possible without contradiction.
Correction: This passage shows that infinite regress would require an infinite chain of gods, each needy and temporally originated, which contradicts the necessary self-sufficiency and power of the Creator.

Checkpoint
What two things does the author refute to prove God's pre-eternity?
A) Circularity and infinite regress
B) Emergence and annihilation
C) Change and motion
D) Need and dependence

Key Takeaway
God's pre-eternity is established because the only alternatives—circularity and infinite regress—are rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever subconsciously believed that God is just one in a long chain of creators, or that there is something eternal besides God? How does this passage force you to abandon that thought?
?
If everything needy and incapable cannot be the creator, then what does that say about your own dependence on other created things? In what areas of your life are you relying on what is needy rather than the Self-Sufficient One?
?
The passage declares that whatever leads to denying God's pre-eternity is impossible. Is there any belief or action in your life that implicitly denies God's eternal nature? What would it mean for you to truly live as if God is the only Pre-Eternal Being?

Allah Does Not Need a Specifier
Proof that Allah does not need a specifier because He is eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's eternality negates the need for any specifier (mukhassis) that would determine His existence or attributes.

Core Idea
Eternity itself excludes the need for a specifier.

This lesson presents a concise argument from Imam al-Dardir: if Allah needed a specifier to determine His existence, He would be temporal (hadith). But since He is eternal (qadim), He is self-sufficient and requires no external cause. This short passage captures a foundational principle of Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence once, then its translation. Notice the key terms: تخصص (specifier), موجد (Existent), مؤثر (Effective).
The passage is very dense; each word carries theological weight.
2
Understand the terminology
The author explains that 'specification' (takhassus) here refers to being the Existent and Effective Being. Why are these two terms used?
In kalam, a specifier is what brings something from non-existence to existence and gives it its specific attributes.
3
Follow the logical implication
The phrase 'فإنه يلزم من الحدوث' indicates that needing a specifier would necessitate temporality. Grasp this cause-effect relationship.
If X needs a specifier, then X is temporal (hadith).
4
Apply the conclusion
Since Allah is pre-eternal (qadim), the antecedent (needing a specifier) is false. The argument is a modus tollens: if P then Q, not Q, therefore not P.
This is a standard proof in kalam for divine self-sufficiency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أنه لا يفتقر إلى تخصص، أي: موجد ومؤثر، فإنه يلزم من الحدوث كما هو في القدم.
And as for His not needing specification, that is, He is the Existent and Effective, then it follows from temporality as is the case in pre-eternity.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a brief statement of the proof that Allah does not need a specifier (mukhassis). The author explains that 'specification' (takhassus) refers to being the Existent and Effective Being. Since lacking specification necessitates temporality (huduth), and Allah is eternal (qadim), He does not need a specifier. In other words, if Allah needed a specifier to determine His existence or attributes, He would be contingent and temporal, but because He is eternal, He is self-sufficient and does not require any external specifier.

Key Terms
تخصص
موجد
مؤثر
حدوث
قدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah's attributes, like His power, require an external cause to be actualized.
Correction: The passage shows that because Allah is eternal, He needs no external specifier for His existence or attributes. His attributes are inherent to His essence (sifat dhatiyya).

Checkpoint
What does the author say about Allah needing a specifier?
A) Allah needs a specifier to manifest His attributes
B) Allah does not need a specifier because He is eternal
C) Allah needs a specifier only for His actions
D) The concept of a specifier is irrelevant

Key Takeaway
Allah's eternality (qidam) proves He has no need for a specifier, unlike temporal beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that Allah does not need a specifier because He is eternal. Do you live as if you truly believe that your existence depends entirely on Him and on no one else? Where in your life do you rely on people or things as if they were the 'specifiers' of your wellbeing?
?
If Allah has no need for anything, then His commands to you are not for His benefit but for yours. Does your obedience reflect that truth, or do you sometimes act as if following Allah is a favor to Him?
?
The proof here is short and clear: needing a specifier would make Allah temporal, but He is eternal. Does this simple logic settle in your heart, or do you still harbor doubts about Allah's self‑sufficiency? What would it take for you to wean your heart from seeking security in creation?
