The Negative Attribute of Oneness (Wahdaniyya)
Imam Dardeer defines the attribute of oneness and explains its three aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the negative attribute of Oneness (Wahdaniyya) as the negation of multiplicity in Allah's essence, attributes, and actions, and specifically the negation of composition in His essence.

Core Idea
Oneness of Allah means no multiplicity and no composition in His essence, attributes, or actions.

Imam Dardeer now explains the fifth negative attribute: Oneness. He begins by defining it as the negation of multiplicity in three domains. Then he focuses on the Oneness of the Essence, showing that it negates both connected and discrete quantity — meaning that Allah is not composed of parts and has no equal. This lesson will walk you through this definition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three domains
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Wahdaniyya negates multiplicity in essence, attributes, and actions. Can you point to the phrase that lists them?
The text says: 'عبارةٌ عَنْ سَلْبِ الكثرة في الذات والصفات والأفعال'.
2
Understand the negation of quantity in the essence
The passage explains that oneness of essence negates both 'connected quantity' (al-kamm al-muttasil) and 'discrete quantity' (al-kamm al-munfasil). Think about what these mean: connected quantity refers to parts joined together (composition), while discrete quantity refers to separate parts (another entity).
3
Follow the proof against composition
Consider why composition is impossible for Allah. The passage gives a brief proof: if His essence were composed of parts, He would be like contingent things and would need a composer. This is impossible. Try to articulate this argument in your own words.
The proof relies on the rule that anything composite requires a composer, which implies dependence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخامسُ الصَّفاتِ السلبية (وحدانية) وهي: عبارةٌ عَنْ سَلْبِ الكثرة في الذات والصفات والأفعال، أي: عدَمُ الاثنينيّةِ (في الذاتِ) أي: في ذاته تعالى اتصالاً وانفصالًا. فوحدانيّةُ الذاتِ تنفي عنه تعالى الكم المتَّصِلَ والمنفَصِلَ، أَيْ: تنفي العدَدَ في الذاتِ، متّصِلا كان أو منفصلا، فتنفي التركيب في ذاته تعالى، ووُجودَ ذات أخرى تُماثِلُ الذات العليّة. أي أنّه تعالى ليستْ ذاتُه مركبةً مِنْ أجزاء متّصل بعضُها ببعض، وإلا لكانَ مُماثلًا للحوادثِ مِنْ حيثُ التركيب، فيحتاجُ إلى مَنْ يُرَكُبُه، وهو مُحالٌ ولَيسَ له نظير في.
And the fifth of the negative attributes is Oneness, and it is: an expression about the negation of multiplicity in the Essence, the attributes, and the actions. That is: the absence of duality (in the Essence) i.e., in His – exalted is He – Essence, in terms of conjunction and separation. So the Oneness of the Essence negates from Him – exalted is He – connected and discrete quantity, i.e., it negates number in the Essence, whether connected or discrete. So it negates composition in His – exalted is He – Essence, and the existence of another essence that resembles the Supreme Essence. That is: His – exalted is He – Essence is not composed of parts connected to one another, otherwise He would be similar to contingent things in terms of composition, and would need someone to compose Him, and that is impossible, and He has no peer in.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth negative attribute: Wahdaniyya (Oneness). The author states that it is the negation of multiplicity (kathrah) in three domains: Essence, attributes, and actions. Specifically, it means the absence of duality (ithnayniyyah) in the Essence, meaning no conjunctive or separative composition. The Oneness of Essence negates both continuous quantity (connected parts) and discrete quantity (separate parts or another entity), thus negating any composition (tarkib) in Allah's Essence and the existence of any other essence resembling His. The proof is given: if His Essence were composed of interconnected parts, He would be similar to contingent things in composition and would need a composer, which is impossible. The passage ends by affirming that He has no peer (nazir), though the text appears cut off.

Key Terms
الوحدانية
سلب الكثرة
الكم المتصل
الكم المنفصل
التركيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that oneness only means no partners, but it also negates composition in the essence and attributes.
Correction: Oneness (Wahdaniyya) negates all multiplicity, including internal composition (tarkib) and the existence of any similar essence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the oneness of Allah's essence negate?
A) Only the existence of other gods.
B) Both connected and discrete quantity in the essence.
C) Only composition in actions.
D) Only multiplicity in attributes.

Key Takeaway
Oneness (Wahdaniyya) negates all multiplicity and composition in Allah's essence, attributes, and actions, affirming His absolute unity and independence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's oneness negates all forms of multiplicity—even within your own understanding of Him—how often do you unknowingly split your heart between Him and the many distractions of this world? What one attachment will you consciously sever today to realign with this truth?
?
The passage argues that composition implies dependence on a composer. Where in your life are you still trying to 'compose' your own identity or salvation by adding parts (status, wealth, relationships) rather than relying solely on the One who is absolutely simple and self-sufficient? What step can you take to rely on Him alone starting this hour?
?
Imam Dardeer says oneness negates multiplicity in Allah's actions. When you look at the events of your past week, do you see them as coming from a single unified divine will, or do you act as if things happen by random coincidence? How would viewing everything as from the One change your response to hardship right now?

Proof of God's Oneness: Burhan al-Tamānu‘
Dardeer presents the proof of mutual exclusion for God's oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof of mutual exclusion (burhān al-tamānu‘) and how it establishes the oneness of God based on the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
The proof of mutual exclusion: if there were multiple gods, the universe would be corrupted.

This lesson introduces one of the most famous arguments in Islamic theology for the oneness of God: the proof of mutual exclusion. Derived from the Quran, this argument shows that multiple deities would inevitably conflict, leading to cosmic disorder. Let's examine how Dardeer presents this concise but powerful proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the immediate meaning.
Notice the Quranic verse reference.
2
Understand the logical structure
The proof argues that if there were multiple gods, their independent wills would conflict, causing corruption in the universe. Since the universe is orderly, there must be only one God.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
The verse from Surah Al-Anbiya (21:22) is presented as evidence. Reflect on how it encapsulates the argument.
This verse is a direct proof from revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشهور في إثباتِ الوحدانيةِ بُرهانُ التمانع، المُشارُ إليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللهُ لَفَسَدَتَا﴾
And the well-known [proof] in establishing oneness is the proof of mutual exclusion (burhān al-tamānu‘), alluded to by His statement, the Exalted: 'If there were in them gods besides God, they would both be corrupted.'
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This brief passage introduces the famous argument for God's oneness known as the proof of mutual exclusion (burhān al-tamānu‘). The argument is derived from the Quranic verse: 'If there were in them [the heavens and the earth] gods besides God, they would both be corrupted.' The logic is that if there were two or more gods, then if they disagreed, one would prevent the other, leading to corruption. The fact that the universe is not corrupted shows there is only one God.

Key Terms
برهان التمانع
وحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof only works if the gods disagree.
Correction: The argument is that independent wills would inevitably conflict, leading to corruption, regardless of specific disagreement.

Checkpoint
What Quranic verse does Dardeer quote as evidence for the proof of mutual exclusion?
A) 'If there were in them gods besides God, they would both be corrupted'
B) 'God is one, God the eternal refuge'
C) 'No god but He, the Mighty, the Wise'
D) 'Had there been gods other than God, they would have sought a way against the Lord of the Throne'

Key Takeaway
The proof of mutual exclusion uses the Quranic verse to show that multiple gods would cause corruption, so only one God exists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that only one God’s will ultimately determines everything, what would change about the way you worry about others’ opinions or fear their rejection? Are there people you ‘worship’ by seeking their approval above His?
?
The proof shows that multiple gods lead to corruption. What are the ‘gods’ in your own heart—desires, habits, or attachments—that you treat as if they have independent power? How are they corrupting your spiritual life, and what will you do today to dethrone them?
?
You recite 'Lā ilāha illa Allāh' daily, but the proof of mutual exclusion demands that you truly accept that no one else shares God’s sovereignty. When you face a difficulty, do you instinctively turn to created means as if they can act independently of Allah? Repent and resolve to rely on Him alone.

Proof of Divine Oneness through Mutual Hindrance
Argument that multiple gods entail possible mutual hindrance, leading to impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutual hindrance (tamānuʿ) argument for divine oneness and why the mere possibility of conflict between multiple gods proves their impossibility.

Core Idea
Multiple gods lead to a possible conflict that ends in logical absurdity.

This lesson presents the classic kalam proof for the oneness of Allah, known as the argument from mutual hindrance. Imam Dardīr, in his commentary, lays out the logical steps: if more than one god existed, they could potentially disagree, and that potential alone results in an impossibility. You will see how the argument handles an important objection and why the conclusion is inescapable.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical structure
The argument begins: if multiple gods were possible, then mutual hindrance would be possible. This is the key premise.
Mutual hindrance means they could will opposite things.
2
Examine the example and three outcomes
Consider a body that one god wills to move and another wills to rest. Both are possible. There are three outcomes: both occur (impossible), neither occurs (implies impotence), or one occurs (implies the other's impotence).
Impotence is a sign of contingency, impossible for God.
3
See how the objection is refuted
An objector says: maybe they always agree. The reply: the mere possibility of hindrance is enough to make multiplicity impossible, regardless of actual agreement.
Possibility itself entails a logical necessity.
4
Connect to the broader lesson on tawḥīd
Therefore, multiplicity is impossible, and only one God can exist. The power to create belongs exclusively to Him.
This argument is a cornerstone of Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصله: أنه لو أمْكَنَ التَّعَدُّدُ لأَمْكَنَ التمانُعُ بَيْنَها، بأنْ يُرِيدَ أحدُهُما حركَ أنا نَها مثلا، والآخَرُ سُكونَه، إذْ كُلُّ منهما أمر ممكن في نفْسِه، وكذا تعلق الإرادة بكُلِّ منها، وحينَئِذٍ إما أن يحصل الأمرانِ، فيلزَمُ اجتِماعُ الضَّدَّين، أو لا، فيلزَمُ عجْزُهما أو عجز أحدهما، وهو أمارة الحدوث والإمكان لما فيه مِنْ شائبة الاحتياج، فالتعدُّدُ مُستلزم لإمكان التمانع، المستلزم للمُحالِ، فيكونُ التعدُّدُ مُحالا. وبها ذكر اندفع ما يُقال: إنه يجوز أن يتفقا مِنْ غَيرِ تمانع، وحاصل الدفع: أن الإمكانَ مُحالٌ وإِنْ لم يقع تمانع بالفعل. وإذا علمت أنه تعالى يجب له الوَحْدانيّةُ فالتأثير الاختراعُ والإيجاد للأشياء مِنَ العدَمِ ليس أي: لا يصِحُ لأحَدٍ إلا للواحِدِ القَهَّارِ وحدَه جل وعلا.
Its summary: if multiplicity were possible, then mutual hindrance between them would be possible, such that one of them wills the movement of something, for example, and the other wills its rest, since each of them is a possible matter in itself, and likewise the attachment of will to each of them. Then either both [willed] occur, necessitating the conjunction of opposites, or they do not, necessitating their impotence or the impotence of one of them, which is a sign of temporality and contingency due to the trace of need in it. Thus multiplicity entails the possibility of mutual hindrance, which entails the impossible, so multiplicity is impossible. And by it [the proof] the objection that it is possible for them to agree without mutual hindrance is repelled. The essence of the repelling: that the possibility itself is impossible even if mutual hindrance does not actually occur. And when you know that Oneness is necessarily due to Him, the Most High, then effecting, invention, and bringing things into existence from non-existence is not correct for anyone except the One, the Subduer, alone, Mighty and Majestic is He.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a proof of divine oneness (tawḥīd) using the well-known kalam argument of mutual hindrance (tamānuʿ). The author begins by stating the logical structure: if there were multiple gods, then mutual hindrance between them would be possible. He gives an example: one god might will the motion of a body while another wills its rest. Both are possible states, and the wills could attach to each. Three outcomes are then considered: either both wills are fulfilled (impossible because opposites cannot coexist), or neither is fulfilled (implying impotence of both or one), which indicates need and thus contingency. Hence multiplicity leads to impossibility. The author then addresses an objection: perhaps the gods could always agree, never hindering each other. He replies that the mere possibility of hindrance is enough to make multiplicity impossible, regardless of actual agreement. Finally, he concludes that since oneness is necessary for the divine, the act of creation (ikhtirāʿ and ījād) belongs only to the One, the Subduer.

Key Terms
التعدد
التمانع
الحدوث
الإمكان
الوحدانية
المحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If multiple gods always agree and never oppose each other, then multiplicity is possible.
Correction: The argument shows that the mere possibility of disagreement (even if never actual) is enough to render multiplicity impossible because possibility itself leads to logical necessity.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the mutual hindrance argument?
A) Multiple gods are impossible.
B) Multiple gods are possible if they agree.
C) Mutual hindrance shows God's power.
D) The example of motion and rest is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The mere logical possibility of conflict between multiple gods proves that only one God can exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly internalized that Allah alone is free from any need and that even the possibility of impotence is absent in Him, how would your fear of created beings diminish? What is one fear of people or circumstances that you need to replace with fear of Allah?
?
The argument shows that multiple gods lead to logical impossibility. Yet in your daily life, you sometimes act as if there are multiple 'gods'—money, status, relationships—that have independent power. Where are you giving created things the authority that belongs only to Allah? Will you repent and realign your heart today?
?
If you believe with certainty that only Allah can create and bring things into existence, then why do you still feel anxious about your provision? What does your anxiety reveal about your actual belief in His sole sovereignty? Commit to a specific dhikr or action that will reinforce this truth in your heart.

God is the Free Agent: Meaning and Refutation of Necessity
Dardeer defines free agent and refutes philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what it means for Allah to be a free agent (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār) and why the philosophers' view that God acts by nature or cause is false.

Core Idea
Allah acts by will, not by necessity or nature.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer explains the meaning of the phrase 'al-fāʿil al-mukhtār' (the free agent) from the matn of al-Kharida. He emphasizes that Allah's actions are voluntary, not compelled by any external nature or cause. This directly opposes the claims of philosophers who assert otherwise and outlines the grave consequences of their error.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of free agent
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that the free agent is defined as 'He who if He wills He does, and if He wills He abandons'. This highlights volition.
2
Contrast with agent by nature or cause
Imam Dardeer explicitly denies that Allah is an agent by nature (al-ṭabʿ) or by cause (al-ʿilla). Understand why these are problematic: they imply compulsion.
The philosophers (falāsifa) are mentioned as holding these views.
3
Identify the consequences of the philosophers' position
The passage states that the philosophers claimed the world is pre-eternal and denied Allah's essential attributes. Reflect on how these follow from their view of a necessary cause.
The pre-eternity of the world (qidam al-ʿālam) is a major point of contention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهو الإله الفاعل المختار
قَولُه (فهْوَ الإِلهُ) أي : المعبودُ بحَقِّ، (الفاعل المختارُ) أي: الذي إِنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَ وَإِنْ شاء ترك، وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختَارُ) لا أنه فاعل بالطبع أو بالعلة، خلاف للفلاسفة الملعونين، ولذا قالوا بقدَمِ العالم، لأنه يلزَمُ مِنْ قِدَمِ العِلَّةِ قِدَمُ المعلول ونفَوا عَن الله تعالى صفاته الذاتية، وهو مذهَبْ باطلٌ وكُفْرٌ مراح، إلى غير ذلك، كما أشار ومما يدلُّ على بطلانه تنوُّعُ العالم إلى أنواع مختلفة، فبعضه جماد، وبعضُه حيوان وبعضُه ظُلْماني، وبعضُه نوران، وبعضُه حُلْو، وبعضُه له الكِتابُ العزيز في كثير مِنَ الآي. قال تعالى: يُسْقَى بِمَاءِ وَاحِدٍ وَنُفَضِّلُ بَعْضَهَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ فِي الْأُكُل إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِّقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ)، فهذا يشير إلى أنَّ هؤلاء الخاسرين ليسوا بعقلاء، إذْ فِعلُ العِلّة والطبيعة ليس إلا شيئًا واحِدًا غَيْرَ مُختلف أَفَلاَ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَى الإِبْل كَيْفَ خُلِقَتْ * وَإِلَى السَّمَاءِ كَيْفَ رُفِعَتْ * وَإِلَى الْجِبَالِ كَيْفَ نُصِبَتْ * وَإِلَى الْأَرْضَ كَيْفَ سُطِحَتْ ، أَفَلَمْ يَنظُرُوا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَوْقَهُمْ كَيْفَ بَنَيْنَاهَا وَزَيَّنَّاهَا وَمَا لَهَا مِن فُرُوج * وَالْأَرْضَ مَدَدْنَاهَا وَأَلْقَيْنَا فِيهَا رَوَاسِيَ وَأَنبَتْنَا فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ ولَكِنْ مَنْ يُضْلِ اللَّهُ فما له مِنْ هَادٍ. ومما بنوه على مذهبهم عدَمُ المعاد الجسماني (ه)، وقد زخرفوا مذاهبهم بشُبَه ظنّيّةٍ خيالية، كسَراب بقيعة يحسبه الظمآن ماءً حتى إذا جاءه لم يجده شَيئًا، فضلوا وأَضَلُّوا حتى ظَنَّ كثيرٌ مِنَ الناسِ أنَّ هذهِ الزخارفَ عِلْمٌ ، بل فضَّلوا المتمسكين بها على عُلماء الشريعة، كلّا سَوفَ يعلمون، ثُمَّ كَلَّا سَوفَ يعلمون.
So He is God, the free agent, the chooser. His statement (so He is God) means: the worshipped with truth, (the free agent) means: He who if He wills He does, and if He wills He abandons. And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses. He is not an agent by nature or by cause, contrary to the accursed philosophers. And therefore they claimed the pre-eternity of the world, because from the pre-eternity of the cause follows the pre-eternity of the effect, and they denied the essential attributes of Allah, exalted is He. And this is a false and blasphemous doctrine, and much else, as he indicated. And among what indicates its falsehood is the diversity of the world into different kinds: some are inanimate, some are animal, some are dark, some are luminous, some are sweet, some are... the Mighty Book has many verses. He said, exalted: 'Watered with one water, and We favor some of them over others in the produce. Indeed in that are signs for people who reason.' So this indicates that these losers are not reasonable, because the action of the cause and nature is only one thing, not diverse. Do they not look at the camel how it was created, and at the sky how it was raised, and at the mountains how they were erected, and at the earth how it was spread out? Did they not look at the sky above them how We built it and adorned it, and it has no cracks, and the earth We extended and cast therein firm mountains and caused to grow therein every beautiful kind? But whoever Allah leads astray has no guide. And among what they built upon their doctrine is the denial of bodily resurrection. They decorated their doctrines with speculative imaginative doubts, like a mirage in a plain which the thirsty thinks is water until when he comes to it he finds nothing. So they went astray and led others astray, until many people thought that these decorations were knowledge. Rather, they preferred those holding to them over the scholars of the Shari'a. No, they will know. Then no, they will know.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of Allah being the 'free agent' (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār) from the matn. The author begins by glossing 'he is God' as 'the worshipped with truth' and 'the free agent' as 'He who does if He wills and refrains if He wills'. This establishes that Allah's actions are not compelled by nature or by a necessary cause, directly opposing the philosophers who claim that God acts by nature (al-ṭabʿ) or by a cause (al-ʿilla). The author then points out the consequences of the philosophers' position: they claim the world is pre-eternal because a pre-eternal cause necessitates a pre-eternal effect, and they deny Allah's essential attributes. This doctrine is labeled false and blasphemous. Next, the author provides a rational proof against their view: the diversity of the world. If the world were the necessary effect of a single cause, it would be uniform. Instead, we observe immense diversity — inanimate and animate, dark and luminous, etc. He quotes Quranic verses (e.g., Surah Raʿd 13:4) to show that this diversity is a sign for rational people, indicating that the action of a cause or nature cannot produce such variety; only a free agent can. He continues with more Quranic exhortations (from Surah al-Ghāshiya and Surah Qāf) calling for reflection on creation. Finally, he mentions another consequence of the philosophers' doctrine: the denial of bodily resurrection (al-maʿād al-jismānī). He dismisses their arguments as mere sophistry and compares them to a mirage. The passage ends with a stern warning: those who prefer such philosophy over the scholars of Shari'a will come to know their error.

Key Terms
الفاعل المختار
الفاعل بالطبع
الفاعل بالعلة
الفلاسفة
قدم العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'free agent' means Allah acts arbitrarily without wisdom.
Correction: The free agent acts according to His will and wisdom; He chooses to do or not do, but His actions are always wise and just.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does it mean for Allah to be a free agent (al-fāʿil al-mukhtār)?
A) He acts by nature
B) He acts by cause
C) He does what He wills and refrains what He wills
D) He is compelled to act

Key Takeaway
The free agent acts by will, not by necessity; denying this leads to false doctrines like the pre-eternity of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own life, do you sometimes feel trapped by circumstances, acting as if you have no choice? How does knowing that Allah is the free agent who acts by will—not by cause or nature—change how you see your own ability to choose and turn to Him?
?
The philosophers denied Allah's attributes because they saw Him as bound by necessity. In your prayer life, do you ever assume Allah will respond in a certain way based on your actions, as if He is bound by cause and effect? What would it mean to truly believe He can choose freely, even when your expectations are not met?
?
If Allah were not free to choose but acted by necessity, supplication (du'a) would be pointless. When you make du'a, do you genuinely believe that Allah can will to grant or withhold based on His wisdom? How does this lesson challenge you to approach du'a with more trust and humility?

The Proof from Diversity and the Denial of Bodily Resurrection
Dardeer presents proof from diversity and warns against denial of bodily resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof from the diversity of creation that demonstrates Allah's free choice, and the consequence of denying bodily resurrection.

Core Idea
The diversity of creation proves the Creator acts by choice, not necessity.

Imam Dardeer continues his refutation of the philosophers by presenting a compelling rational argument: the world is full of diversity, but a necessary cause would produce only uniform effects. He then points out another grave error of the philosophers—their denial of bodily resurrection—and warns against being deceived by their sophistry.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof from diversity
Read the author's argument: if the world were the necessary effect of a single cause, it would be uniform. But we see immense diversity—animate/inanimate, dark/luminous, etc. This diversity can only come from a free agent.
He quotes Quranic verses to support this, e.g., Surah Raʿd 13:4 about fruits from one water.
2
Reflect on the Quranic exhortations
The author cites additional verses calling for reflection on creation (camel, sky, mountains, earth). These are meant to awaken the intellect.
3
Identify another consequence: denial of bodily resurrection
The philosophers also deny bodily resurrection based on their doctrine. The author dismisses their arguments as imaginative doubts, like a mirage.
He warns that many people were deceived by their philosophical sophistry.
4
Note the stern warning at the end
The passage ends with a threat: 'No, they will know. Then no, they will know.' This is a strong condemnation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهو الإله الفاعل المختار
قَولُه (فهْوَ الإِلهُ) أي : المعبودُ بحَقِّ، (الفاعل المختارُ) أي: الذي إِنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَ وَإِنْ شاء ترك، وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختَارُ) لا أنه فاعل بالطبع أو بالعلة، خلاف للفلاسفة الملعونين، ولذا قالوا بقدَمِ العالم، لأنه يلزَمُ مِنْ قِدَمِ العِلَّةِ قِدَمُ المعلول ونفَوا عَن الله تعالى صفاته الذاتية، وهو مذهَبْ باطلٌ وكُفْرٌ مراح، إلى غير ذلك، كما أشار ومما يدلُّ على بطلانه تنوُّعُ العالم إلى أنواع مختلفة، فبعضه جماد، وبعضُه حيوان وبعضُه ظُلْماني، وبعضُه نوران، وبعضُه حُلْو، وبعضُه له الكِتابُ العزيز في كثير مِنَ الآي. قال تعالى: يُسْقَى بِمَاءِ وَاحِدٍ وَنُفَضِّلُ بَعْضَهَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ فِي الْأُكُل إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِّقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ)، فهذا يشير إلى أنَّ هؤلاء الخاسرين ليسوا بعقلاء، إذْ فِعلُ العِلّة والطبيعة ليس إلا شيئًا واحِدًا غَيْرَ مُختلف أَفَلاَ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَى الإِبْل كَيْفَ خُلِقَتْ * وَإِلَى السَّمَاءِ كَيْفَ رُفِعَتْ * وَإِلَى الْجِبَالِ كَيْفَ نُصِبَتْ * وَإِلَى الْأَرْضَ كَيْفَ سُطِحَتْ ، أَفَلَمْ يَنظُرُوا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَوْقَهُمْ كَيْفَ بَنَيْنَاهَا وَزَيَّنَّاهَا وَمَا لَهَا مِن فُرُوج * وَالْأَرْضَ مَدَدْنَاهَا وَأَلْقَيْنَا فِيهَا رَوَاسِيَ وَأَنبَتْنَا فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ ولَكِنْ مَنْ يُضْلِ اللَّهُ فما له مِنْ هَادٍ. ومما بنوه على مذهبهم عدَمُ المعاد الجسماني (ه)، وقد زخرفوا مذاهبهم بشُبَه ظنّيّةٍ خيالية، كسَراب بقيعة يحسبه الظمآن ماءً حتى إذا جاءه لم يجده شَيئًا، فضلوا وأَضَلُّوا حتى ظَنَّ كثيرٌ مِنَ الناسِ أنَّ هذهِ الزخارفَ عِلْمٌ ، بل فضَّلوا المتمسكين بها على عُلماء الشريعة، كلّا سَوفَ يعلمون، ثُمَّ كَلَّا سَوفَ يعلمون.
So He is God, the free agent, the chooser. His statement (so He is God) means: the worshipped with truth, (the free agent) means: He who if He wills He does, and if He wills He abandons. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the diversity of the world could still arise from a single necessary cause if that cause is complex.
Correction: A necessary cause produces only one effect; diversity of effects requires a cause with multiple attributes or a free agent who chooses different outcomes.

What is the main proof given in this passage against the philosophers' claim that God acts by nature or by cause?
A) The pre-eternity of the world

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers denied bodily resurrection based on their own reasoning. Is there any Islamic belief you have ever doubted because it didn't fit your logic? How can you submit your intellect to revelation while still using reason properly?
?
The diversity of creation is a sign for those who reason. When was the last time you truly paused to reflect on the variety in Allah's creation—animals, plants, colors, and forms—and let it increase your faith in His wisdom and choice? What distracts you from such reflection?
?
Dardeer warns that many people preferred the eloquent philosophers over the true scholars. In your pursuit of knowledge, have you ever been attracted to a speaker or writer whose words sound profound but contradict sound Islamic teachings? How can you protect yourself from being deceived by 'decorated' falsehood?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
5 min
Attributes from Self-Sufficiency
Dardeer derives essential attributes from Allah's self-sufficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how self-sufficiency (istighna') implies the essential attributes of existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, dissimilarity to originated things, self-subsistence, and the perfect attributes of hearing, sight, and speech.

Core Idea
Self-sufficiency is the key that unlocks the essential divine attributes.

In this passage, Imam al-Dardeer explains that the first part of the kalima, 'La ilaha illallah,' implies that Allah is absolutely independent of everything else. From this self-sufficiency, he derives a series of necessary attributes. Let's see how each attribute follows logically from the concept of independence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully and note the two major sections: the direct attributes and the implications of transcendence.
Focus on the logical connectors like 'فـ' and 'إذ'.
2
Identify the derived attributes
List the attributes directly necessitated by self-sufficiency: existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, dissimilarity, self-subsistence.
Also notice the arguments against resemblance and dependence.
3
Understand transcendence and perfections
See how self-sufficiency leads to transcendence above imperfections, which in turn necessitates hearing, sight, and speech, and negates purposes in actions.
Consider why lacking these would imply neediness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما استغناؤه عنْ كُلِّ ما سواه فيوجِبُ له تعالى الوُجودَ والقِدَمَ والبقاء ومُخالفته تعالى للحوادث وقيامه بنَفْسِه، إذ لو ماثل شَيئًا منها للَزِمَه ما لزِمَهَا مِنَ الافتِقارِ وهو مُحالٌ، ولو قامَ بِغَيرِه لكان مُفتقِرًا إلى ذلك الغَيرِ. ويوجِبُ له أيضًا التنزه عن النقائص، وهو يستلْزِمُ وُجوبَ السَّمْعِ والبَصَرِ والكلام، والتنَزَّهِ عنِ الأغراض في الأفعالِ والأحكام، وإلا لكانَ مُفْتَقَرًا إلى ما يُتكَمَّلُ بِه مِنْ ذلكَ العَرَضِ، وعدَمَ وُجوبِ فِعلِ شَيْءٍ مِنَ المُمكِناتِ أَو تَرْكِه، وعدَمَ كَونِ شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ يُؤْثِرُ بِقُوَّةٍ أَوْدَعَهَا اللَّهَ فِيه، وإلا لَمْ يَكُنَّ مُسْتَغْنِيَا عَنْ كُلِّ ما سواه، كَيفَ وهو الغني بالإطلاقِ عنْ كُلِّ ما سواه. وأما افتقارُ كُل ما سواه إليه تعالى، فهو يوجِبُ له تعالى القُدْرةَ والإرادة والعِلْمَ والحياة والوحدانية؛ لِما تقدَّمَ مِنْ أنَّ التعدُّدَ يوجِبُ العجْزَ. ويؤخَذُ منه حُدوثُ العالَم بأسره، ونفي تأثير شَيءٍ منه بالطبع أو بالعِلّة، وإذا وجَبَ شَيْءٌ استحالَ ضِدُّه. هذا حاصل ما بيَّنَه الإمامُ السُّنوسي رَضِي الله عَنْهُ. ولك أن تقول: اللهُ علَمٌ على الذّاتِ الواجب الوجودِ، الخالقِ للعالم، وقد دلّتْ هذه الجملة على حضر الألوهية فيه تعالى، وظاهَرٌ أَنَّ كَونَه واجبَ الوُجودِ وخالقا للعالم يتضمن جميع ما ذكر.
As for His self-sufficiency from everything other than Him, it necessitates for Him, exalted, existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, His being different from originated things, and His self-subsistence. For if He resembled anything of them, what befell them of need would befall Him, which is impossible. And if He subsisted by other than Himself, He would be dependent on that other. And it also necessitates for Him transcendence above imperfections, and that necessitates the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech, and transcendence above purposes (aghrad) in actions and rulings, otherwise He would be dependent on that which perfects Him through that accident. And it necessitates the non-necessity of doing or refraining from any possible thing, and the non-being of any possible thing having influence by a power lodged in it by Allah, otherwise He would not be independent of everything else, how so, while He is absolutely independent of everything else. And as for the dependence of everything else upon Him, it necessitates for Him, exalted, power, will, knowledge, life, and unity; because of what preceded that multiplicity necessitates incapacity. And from it is taken the origination of the entire world, and the negation of any influence of anything from it by nature or by cause, and when a thing is necessary, its opposite is impossible. This is the gist of what Imam al-Sanusi explained, may Allah be pleased with him. And you may say: 'Allah' is a proper noun for the essence that is necessarily existent, the creator of the world, and this sentence has indicated the presence of divinity in Him, exalted, and it is apparent that His being necessarily existent and creator of the world includes all that was mentioned.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof (istidlal) that derives the essential attributes of Allah from the two implications of the first sentence of the Kalima: (1) Allah's self-sufficiency (istighna') and (2) the dependence (iftiqar) of everything else upon Him. The author first explains the implications of self-sufficiency. From it, he derives the attributes of existence (wujud), pre-eternity (qidam), everlastingness (baqa'), being different from originated things (mukhalafat li-l-hawadith), and self-subsistence (qiyam bi-nafsi). He argues that if Allah resembled any contingent thing, He would share its neediness, which is impossible. If He subsisted by another, He would be dependent. Self-sufficiency also entails transcendence (tanzih) above imperfections, which in turn necessitates the attributes of hearing (sam'), sight (basar), and speech (kalam), and transcendence above purposes (aghrad) in actions and rulings—since otherwise He would be dependent on something else for perfection. Moreover, self-sufficiency implies that He is not obligated to do or refrain from any possible thing, and that no possible thing can have inherent power of influence independently of Allah, because that would undermine His absolute independence. Second, from the dependence of everything else upon Allah, the author derives the attributes of power (qudra), will (irada), knowledge ('ilm), life (hayat), and unity (wahdaniyya). The basis for unity is that multiplicity would imply incapacity. From this dependence also follows the temporal origination (huduth) of the entire world, the negation of natural or causal influence in created things, and the principle that when something is necessary, its opposite is impossible. The author concludes by attributing this summary to Imam al-Sanusi, then offers an alternative concise formulation: one could say that 'Allah' is a proper noun for the necessarily existent Essence that created the world, and this name indicates the presence of divinity and implicitly includes all the attributes derived above.

Key Terms
استغناء
وجود
قدم
بقاء
مخالفة للحوادث
قيام بالنفس
تنزه عن النقائص
سمع
بصر
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah might be similar to created beings or need something.
Correction: Self-sufficiency logically entails dissimilarity and independence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT directly necessitated by self-sufficiency according to the passage?
A) Existence
B) Pre-eternity
C) Power
D) Self-subsistence

Key Takeaway
Self-sufficiency is the foundational attribute from which the essential attributes of existence, pre-eternity, dissimilarity, self-subsistence, and perfections like hearing and speech are derived.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly acknowledge that your existence, every breath, and every ability is a gift from the Self-Sufficient One? How would your daily attitude change if you lived with constant awareness of your absolute need for Him?
?
If Allah is absolutely independent of you, why does He command your worship? Will you obey out of love and recognition of His perfection, or out of habit and comfort?
?
This lesson shows that Allah's attributes are not arbitrary but logically necessary from His self-sufficiency. Are you willing to trust that His commands are perfect and free from any need, even when you don't understand them? What area of your life needs that trust right now?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
5 min
Attributes from the Dependence of Creation
Dardeer derives active attributes from creation's dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dependence (iftiqar) of everything else upon Allah necessitates the attributes of power, will, knowledge, life, and unity, and also implies the origination of the world and the negation of natural causation.

Core Idea
Everything's need for Allah proves His attributes of perfection and absolute uniqueness.

After establishing Allah's self-sufficiency, Imam al-Dardeer now turns to the other side of the divine relationship: the utter dependence of all creation upon Him. This dependence, he argues, necessitates a set of active attributes in Allah, and also reveals the created nature of the world and the impossibility of any created thing having inherent causal power.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage focusing on the list of attributes derived from dependence.
Notice the phrase 'لما تقدم من أن التعدد يوجب العجز'.
2
Identify the derived attributes
List the attributes: power, will, knowledge, life, and unity. Understand the link to unity via the impossibility of multiplicity.
Why does multiplicity imply incapacity?
3
Examine the implications
Note the additional points: the world is originated (huduth), no natural or causal influence in creation, and the logical principle that what is necessary excludes its opposite.
These are direct consequences of dependence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما استغناؤه عنْ كُلِّ ما سواه فيوجِبُ له تعالى الوُجودَ والقِدَمَ والبقاء ومُخالفته تعالى للحوادث وقيامه بنَفْسِه، إذ لو ماثل شَيئًا منها للَزِمَه ما لزِمَهَا مِنَ الافتِقارِ وهو مُحالٌ، ولو قامَ بِغَيرِه لكان مُفتقِرًا إلى ذلك الغَيرِ. ويوجِبُ له أيضًا التنزه عن النقائص، وهو يستلْزِمُ وُجوبَ السَّمْعِ والبَصَرِ والكلام، والتنَزَّهِ عنِ الأغراض في الأفعالِ والأحكام، وإلا لكانَ مُفْتَقَرًا إلى ما يُتكَمَّلُ بِه مِنْ ذلكَ العَرَضِ، وعدَمَ وُجوبِ فِعلِ شَيْءٍ مِنَ المُمكِناتِ أَو تَرْكِه، وعدَمَ كَونِ شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ يُؤْثِرُ بِقُوَّةٍ أَوْدَعَهَا اللَّهَ فِيه، وإلا لَمْ يَكُنَّ مُسْتَغْنِيَا عَنْ كُلِّ ما سواه، كَيفَ وهو الغني بالإطلاقِ عنْ كُلِّ ما سواه. وأما افتقارُ كُل ما سواه إليه تعالى، فهو يوجِبُ له تعالى القُدْرةَ والإرادة والعِلْمَ والحياة والوحدانية؛ لِما تقدَّمَ مِنْ أنَّ التعدُّدَ يوجِبُ العجْزَ. ويؤخَذُ منه حُدوثُ العالَم بأسره، ونفي تأثير شَيءٍ منه بالطبع أو بالعِلّة، وإذا وجَبَ شَيْءٌ استحالَ ضِدُّه. هذا حاصل ما بيَّنَه الإمامُ السُّنوسي رَضِي الله عَنْهُ. ولك أن تقول: اللهُ علَمٌ على الذّاتِ الواجب الوجودِ، الخالقِ للعالم، وقد دلّتْ هذه الجملة على حضر الألوهية فيه تعالى، وظاهَرٌ أَنَّ كَونَه واجبَ الوُجودِ وخالقا للعالم يتضمن جميع ما ذكر.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the world could be eternal or that created things have inherent causal power.
Correction: Dependence on Allah implies temporal origination and negates inherent causality in creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which attribute is NOT directly necessitated by the dependence of creation?
A) Power
B) Will
C) Eternity
D) Unity

Key Takeaway
Creation's total dependence on Allah proves that He alone is powerful, knowing, living, and one, and that everything other than Him is originated and causally inert.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if everything depends on Allah, or do you sometimes feel self-sufficient and forget your constant need for His power, will, and knowledge? What practical change can you make today to acknowledge your dependence?
?
When you recognize that your own abilities are given by Allah and have no inherent power, does that humble you or make you feel helpless? How can you turn that feeling into deeper trust in Him?
?
If you sincerely believed that nothing in creation can influence your life except by Allah's leave, how would your fear of people and your hope in them change? What specific fear can you work on surrendering right now?

Allah's Existence
beginner
3 min
The Kalima as a Comprehensive Proof
Dardeer summarizes and offers a concise alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the kalima 'La ilaha illallah' contains within it the entire proof for the divine attributes, and how the name 'Allah' itself indicates the necessarily existent creator.

Core Idea
The entire creed is contained in the first part of the kalima.

Imam al-Dardeer concludes by summarizing that everything derived above is encapsulated in the first sentence of the kalima. He also offers an alternative formulation: the name 'Allah' is a proper noun for the essence that is necessarily existent and creator of the world, which implicitly includes all the attributes discussed.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding passage
Read the Arabic passage noting the attribution to Imam al-Sanusi and the alternative formulation.
The phrase 'ولك أن تقول' introduces the concise version.
2
Understand the concise formulation
Realize that 'Allah' is a proper noun for the necessarily existent creator, and this implies all attributes.
How does 'necessary existence' imply self-sufficiency? How does 'creator' imply power, will, etc.?
3
Reflect on comprehensiveness
Think about how the kalima alone can be a complete statement of tawhid.
This shows the depth of the testimony of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما استغناؤه عنْ كُلِّ ما سواه فيوجِبُ له تعالى الوُجودَ والقِدَمَ والبقاء ومُخالفته تعالى للحوادث وقيامه بنَفْسِه، إذ لو ماثل شَيئًا منها للَزِمَه ما لزِمَهَا مِنَ الافتِقارِ وهو مُحالٌ، ولو قامَ بِغَيرِه لكان مُفتقِرًا إلى ذلك الغَيرِ. ويوجِبُ له أيضًا التنزه عن النقائص، وهو يستلْزِمُ وُجوبَ السَّمْعِ والبَصَرِ والكلام، والتنَزَّهِ عنِ الأغراض في الأفعالِ والأحكام، وإلا لكانَ مُفْتَقَرًا إلى ما يُتكَمَّلُ بِه مِنْ ذلكَ العَرَضِ، وعدَمَ وُجوبِ فِعلِ شَيْءٍ مِنَ المُمكِناتِ أَو تَرْكِه، وعدَمَ كَونِ شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ يُؤْثِرُ بِقُوَّةٍ أَوْدَعَهَا اللَّهَ فِيه، وإلا لَمْ يَكُنَّ مُسْتَغْنِيَا عَنْ كُلِّ ما سواه، كَيفَ وهو الغني بالإطلاقِ عنْ كُلِّ ما سواه. وأما افتقارُ كُل ما سواه إليه تعالى، فهو يوجِبُ له تعالى القُدْرةَ والإرادة والعِلْمَ والحياة والوحدانية؛ لِما تقدَّمَ مِنْ أنَّ التعدُّدَ يوجِبُ العجْزَ. ويؤخَذُ منه حُدوثُ العالَم بأسره، ونفي تأثير شَيءٍ منه بالطبع أو بالعِلّة، وإذا وجَبَ شَيْءٌ استحالَ ضِدُّه. هذا حاصل ما بيَّنَه الإمامُ السُّنوسي رَضِي الله عَنْهُ. ولك أن تقول: اللهُ علَمٌ على الذّاتِ الواجب الوجودِ، الخالقِ للعالم، وقد دلّتْ هذه الجملة على حضر الألوهية فيه تعالى، وظاهَرٌ أَنَّ كَونَه واجبَ الوُجودِ وخالقا للعالم يتضمن جميع ما ذكر.
As for His self-sufficiency from everything other than Him, it necessitates for Him, exalted, existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, His being different from originated things, and His self-subsistence. For if He resembled anything of them, what befell them of need would befall Him, which is impossible. And if He subsisted by other than Himself, He would be dependent on that other. Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof (istidlal) that derives the essential attributes of Allah from the two implications of the first sentence of the Kalima: (1) Allah's self-sufficiency (istighna') and (2) the dependence (iftiqar) of everything else upon Him. Checkpoint
According to the passage, the name 'Allah' is a proper noun for which essence?
A) The essence that is necessarily existent
B) The essence that is contingent
C) The essence that is unknown
D) The essence that has partners

Key Takeaway
The kalima and the name 'Allah' are complete statements that entail all divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah' in your prayers or daily speech, do you consciously recognize that this one name contains everything you believe about Him—His self-sufficiency, power, knowledge, and mercy? What would change in your heart if you paused to reflect on that comprehensiveness each time you utter His name?
?
If someone asked you to prove that Allah has all perfect attributes using only the first part of the kalima ('لا إله إلا الله'), could you do it? What does your ability or inability reveal about how deeply you have internalized this lesson?
?
This lesson shows that our entire creed is summarized in a single phrase. How does this simplicity confront the distractions and multiplicity of your daily concerns? What is one concrete step you can take today to live as if 'Allah is enough'—not just as a statement but as a reality that shapes your priorities?
